Divine Attributes
beginner
6 min
Obligatory Beliefs About God
Lists obligatory beliefs about God's unity and attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fundamental beliefs about God's unity, attributes, and transcendence that every Muslim must affirm.

Core Idea
God is One, unique in essence and attributes, and absolutely unlike His creation.

This passage from Imam al-Ghazali outlines the core obligatory beliefs about Allah. It begins with the oneness of God's essence and divinity, then affirms His essential attributes of life, power, knowledge, will, hearing, sight, and speech—all while emphasizing that His attributes are utterly unlike those of created beings. Understanding these points is essential for a sound Islamic creed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation.
Read the Arabic passage once through, then read the literal translation to get the full meaning.
Pay attention to the structure: it starts with 'As for what is believed as obligatory...' and ends with 'This is what is believed as obligatory.'
2
Identify the main categories of belief.
The passage moves from oneness to essential attributes (life, self-subsistence), then to power, knowledge, will, and finally the sensory attributes of hearing, sight, and speech. Note the repeated emphasis on transcendence.
Each category is introduced by 'and that' (وأنه) in the Arabic.
3
Note the emphasis on incomparability.
The passage stresses that God's attributes do not resemble attributes of creation, just as His essence does not resemble essences. The verse 'Nothing is like Him' is quoted at the end.
This guards against anthropomorphism.
4
Reflect on why both attributes and transcendence are affirmed together.
Ghazali affirms real attributes but denies any similarity to created things. This balances affirming God's perfection while protecting His uniqueness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما ما يعتقد وجوبه : فهو أن تعتقد أن الله سبحانه وتعالى واحد غير منقسم في ذاته ، وأنه ليس معه ثان في إلاهيته ، وأنه حي قيوم ، لا تأخذه سنة ولا نوم ، وأنه إله كل شيء وخالقه ، وأنه على كل شيء قدير ، وأنه عالم بما ظهر وما بطن ، لا يعزب عنه مثقال ذرة في السموات ولا في الأرض ، وأنه مريد لكل كائن من خير أو شر ، ما شاء كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن ، وأنه سميع بصير ، متكلم بغير جارحة ولا آلة ، بل سمعه وبصره وكلامه صفات له ، لا تشبه صفاته الصفات ، كما لا تشبه ذاته الذوات ليس كمثله شيء وهو السميع البصير
هذا ما يعتقد وجوبه
As for what is believed as obligatory: it is that you believe that Allah, glorified and exalted, is One, not divided in His essence, and that there is no second with Him in His divinity, and that He is Living, Self-Subsisting, slumber does not overtake Him nor sleep, and that He is the God of everything and its Creator, and that He is over all things Powerful, and that He is Knower of what is apparent and what is hidden, not escaping Him the weight of an atom in the heavens nor in the earth, and that He is Willing for every existent thing, good or evil, what He wills is and what He does not will is not, and that He is Hearing, Seeing, Speaking without a limb or instrument, rather His hearing, sight, and speech are attributes of Him, His attributes do not resemble attributes, just as His essence does not resemble essences, there is nothing like Him, and He is the Hearing, the Seeing. This is what is believed as obligatory.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage details the first category of creedal details: what must be believed as obligatory (wajib). It begins with the oneness of God: He is one, not divided in essence, and has no partner in divinity. Then it affirms His essential attributes: He is Living and Self-Subsisting (Hayy Qayyum), free from the infirmities of sleep. He is the God and Creator of all things, all-powerful, all-knowing with knowledge encompassing the hidden and apparent. His will is universal: all that occurs, good or evil, happens by His will. Then it affirms His attributes of hearing, sight, and speech, emphasizing that these are real attributes but not like those of creatures—they are without limbs or instruments. The passage stresses that God's attributes are incomparable to any other attributes, just as His essence is incomparable. It concludes by stating that this is the obligatory belief.

Key Terms
وجوب
واحد
حي قيوم
صفات
سميع
بصير
متكلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's attributes of hearing, sight, and speech are like human attributes, involving physical organs.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that God hears, sees, and speaks without limbs or instruments, and His attributes do not resemble any created attributes.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which attribute of God is affirmed without a limb or instrument?
A) Power
B) Will
C) Speech
D) Knowledge

Key Takeaway
Affirming God's oneness, perfect attributes, and absolute transcendence is the core of Islamic creed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If nothing happens except by Allah's will, including the evil you witness, how does that change your attitude toward suffering? What do you need to say to Allah about it?
?
When you think of Allah's attributes—His seeing, hearing, power—do you catch yourself picturing them like human abilities? What step will you take today to purify your belief in tanzih?
?
Allah knows even the hidden weight of an atom. Knowing that, what secret thought or habit are you most afraid He sees? Will you repent from it now or continue hiding?

Divine Attributes

God's Eternality and Independence
Lists impossibilities related to God's eternality and independence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God is necessarily eternal, without beginning or end, and independent of all creation.

Core Idea
God is the eternal, self-sufficient First and Last.

Imam Ghazali begins by establishing the fundamental impossibilities regarding God's existence. The first set of impossibilities affirms that God cannot be temporal or non-existent; He is pre-eternal and everlasting. This lesson explores the logical foundation of God's eternality and His complete independence from creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to get the overall meaning.
Notice the emphatic tone of denial.
2
Identify the impossibilities listed
The passage denies originatedness (huduth) and non-existence ('adam) for God. Also note the affirmations: pre-eternal, everlasting, no beginning/end, First/Last.
These are all necessary attributes of God.
3
Reflect on divine independence
The passage also states that God is independent of creation and needs no supporter. Connect this to the concept of as-samad (self-sufficient).
Independence is a corollary of eternality.
4
Connect to the broader kalam framework
Ask yourself: Why is it necessary to deny originatedness for God? How does this lead to the argument for His oneness?
This sets the stage for the next lessons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما ما يعتقد استحالته ، فهو : أن تعتقد أنه تعالى يستحيل عليه الحدوث ، والعدم ، بل هو تعالى بصفاته وأسمائه ، قديم باق ، دائم الوجود ، قائم على كل نفس بما كسبت ، ليس له أول ولا آخر ، بل هو الأول والآخر ، وأنه لا إله سواه ، لو كان فيهما آلهة إلا الله لفسدتا ، وأنه مستغن عن جميع خلقه ، غير محتاج الى ظهير في ملكه ، وأنه لا يشغله شأن عن شأن في قضائه وأمره ، وأنه لا يحويه مكان في سمواته ولا أرضه ، بل هو كما كان قبل خلق المكان ، وأنه ليس بجوهر ولا جسم ولا على صورة ولا شكل ، ولا له شبيه ولا مثل ، بل هو الأحد الصمد الذي لم يلد ولم يولد ولم يكن له كفوا أحد ،
وأنه لا تحله الحوادث والتغيرات ، ولا تلحقه النقائض والآفات ، وأنه لا يليق به الظلم ، بل قضاؤه كله حكمة وعدل ، وأنه ليس شيء من أفعال خليقته بغير قضائه وخلقه وارادته ، بل :
وَتَمَّتْ كَلِمَةُ رَبِّكَ صِدْقاً وَعَدْلاً ، لا مُبَدِّلَ لِكَلِمَاتِهِ ) )
يُضِلُّ مَنْ يَشَاءُ وَيَهْدِي مَنْ يَشَاءُ )
As for what is believed as impossible: it is that you believe that it is impossible for Him, exalted, to have originatedness and non-existence; rather He, exalted, with His attributes and names, is pre-eternal, everlasting, perpetual in existence, standing over every soul for what it has earned; He has no beginning nor end; rather He is the First and the Last; and that there is no god but Him; if there were in them two gods besides Allah, they would both be corrupted; and that He is independent of all His creation, not in need of a supporter in His kingdom; and that no affair distracts Him from another in His decree and command; and that no place contains Him in His heavens nor His earth; rather He is as He was before the creation of place; and that He is not a substance nor a body nor in a form nor a shape; and there is no peer nor likeness for Him; rather He is the One, the Eternal Refuge, who neither begets nor is begotten, nor is there to Him any equivalent. And that events and changes do not befall Him, nor deficiencies and afflictions overtake Him; and that injustice is not befitting to Him; rather His decree is all wisdom and justice; and that nothing of the actions of His creation occurs without His decree, creation, and will; rather: 'And the word of your Lord has been fulfilled in truth and justice; none can alter His words' (Qur'an 6:115), 'He leads astray whom He wills and guides whom He wills' (Qur'an 16:93).
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage details the second category: what must be believed as impossible (mustahil). It begins by denying that God could have originatedness (huduth) or non-existence ('adam); He is pre-eternal (qadim) and everlasting (baqi). He has no beginning or end; He is the First and the Last. Then it affirms the impossibility of any other god, citing the Qur'anic argument that if there were two gods besides Allah (i.e., multiple gods), the heavens and earth would be corrupted (Qur'an 21:22). God is independent (mustaghni) and needs no helper. He is not contained by any place; He existed before the creation of place. Then it denies that God is a substance (jawhar), a body (jism), or has a form or shape. There is no one like Him; He is the One (Ahad), the Self-Sufficient (Samad), who neither begets nor is begotten. Furthermore, events and changes do not occur in Him, nor do deficiencies or afflictions. Injustice is impossible for Him; His decree is all wisdom and justice. Finally, it affirms that all actions of creation occur by His decree, creation, and will, quoting two verses to emphasize that His word is truth and that He guides and leads astray as He wills.

Key Terms
استحالة
حدوث
عدم
قديم
باق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Believing that God could have originated (come into existence) or that He could cease to exist.
Correction: God is necessarily pre-eternal and everlasting; originatedness and non-existence are impossible for Him.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is stated as impossible for God in this passage?
A) Being eternal
B) Being independent
C) Having originatedness
D) Being the First

Key Takeaway
God is necessarily eternal, without beginning or end, and completely independent of all creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God is completely independent and self-sufficient, why do you often live as though He needs your worship or as though your actions add something to His kingdom? How does this truth challenge the way you seek His pleasure?
?
Because God is the First and the Last, without beginning or end, your entire life is a mere breath between two eternities. Are you living today as if this fleeting moment matters for the Eternal?
?
The passage says God needs no helper in His kingdom. Is there an area of your life where you are relying on someone or something other than the Self‑Sufficient One to give you security, identity, or meaning? What concrete step can you take today to redirect that trust to Him alone?

Divine Attributes

God's Transcendence Beyond Space and Form
Lists impossibilities related to God's transcendence over physical attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God transcends all physical categories: He is not a body, substance, or form, and is not confined by place.

Core Idea
God is not a body, substance, or form, nor is He contained by space.

Having established God's eternality, Imam Ghazali now clarifies that God is absolutely unlike any created being. He cannot be described in physical terms such as substance or body, nor is He limited by location. This lesson explores the positive declaration that God is the One, the Eternal Refuge, who neither begets nor is begotten.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Note the sequence of denials.
The passage builds a wall of negation around God's transcendence.
2
List the negations
Identify each thing denied of God: containment in place, substance, body, form, shape, peer, likeness, begetting, being begotten, events and changes, deficiencies.
This is a comprehensive list.
3
Understand the positive affirmations
God is al-Ahad (the One) and as-Samad (the Eternal Refuge). Explore the meanings of these names.
These names encapsulate His uniqueness and self-sufficiency.
4
Reflect on qadr
The passage also denies that events and changes occur in God. Connect this to divine immutability.
God is not subject to time or change.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما ما يعتقد استحالته ، فهو : أن تعتقد أنه تعالى يستحيل عليه الحدوث ، والعدم ، بل هو تعالى بصفاته وأسمائه ، قديم باق ، دائم الوجود ، قائم على كل نفس بما كسبت ، ليس له أول ولا آخر ، بل هو الأول والآخر ، وأنه لا إله سواه ، لو كان فيهما آلهة إلا الله لفسدتا ، وأنه مستغن عن جميع خلقه ، غير محتاج الى ظهير في ملكه ، وأنه لا يشغله شأن عن شأن في قضائه وأمره ، وأنه لا يحويه مكان في سمواته ولا أرضه ، بل هو كما كان قبل خلق المكان ، وأنه ليس بجوهر ولا جسم ولا على صورة ولا شكل ، ولا له شبيه ولا مثل ، بل هو الأحد الصمد الذي لم يلد ولم يولد ولم يكن له كفوا أحد ،
وأنه لا تحله الحوادث والتغيرات ، ولا تلحقه النقائض والآفات ، وأنه لا يليق به الظلم ، بل قضاؤه كله حكمة وعدل ، وأنه ليس شيء من أفعال خليقته بغير قضائه وخلقه وارادته ، بل :
وَتَمَّتْ كَلِمَةُ رَبِّكَ صِدْقاً وَعَدْلاً ، لا مُبَدِّلَ لِكَلِمَاتِهِ ) )
يُضِلُّ مَنْ يَشَاءُ وَيَهْدِي مَنْ يَشَاءُ )
As for what is believed as impossible: it is that you believe that it is impossible for Him, exalted, to have originatedness and non-existence; rather He, exalted, with His attributes and names, is pre-eternal, everlasting, perpetual in existence, standing over every soul for what it has earned; He has no beginning nor end; rather He is the First and the Last; and that there is no god but Him; if there were in them two gods besides Allah, they would both be corrupted; and that He is independent of all His creation, not in need of a supporter in His kingdom; and that no affair distracts Him from another in His decree and command; and that no place contains Him in His heavens nor His earth; rather He is as He was before the creation of place; and that He is not a substance nor a body nor in a form nor a shape; and there is no peer nor likeness for Him; rather He is the One, the Eternal Refuge, who neither begets nor is begotten, nor is there to Him any equivalent. And that events and changes do not befall Him, nor deficiencies and afflictions overtake Him; and that injustice is not befitting to Him; rather His decree is all wisdom and justice; and that nothing of the actions of His creation occurs without His decree, creation, and will; rather: 'And the word of your Lord has been fulfilled in truth and justice; none can alter His words' (Qur'an 6:115), 'He leads astray whom He wills and guides whom He wills' (Qur'an 16:93).
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage details the second category: what must be believed as impossible (mustahil). It begins by denying that God could have originatedness (huduth) or non-existence ('adam); He is pre-eternal (qadim) and everlasting (baqi). He has no beginning or end; He is the First and the Last. Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that God is a physical being or that He occupies space in heaven.
Correction: God is not a body, substance, or form, and no place contains Him; He is transcendent.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which of the following is impossible for God?
A) Being eternal
B) Being contained by place
C) Having knowledge
D) Being independent

Key Takeaway
God is completely transcendent: He is not a body, not confined by space, and has no peer or likeness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage says no affair distracts God from another. In your life, do you act as if God's attention is divided, or do you entrust all your concerns to Him simultaneously without fearing He might miss one? What would change if you truly believed this?
?
If God is not contained by any place, have you ever felt His presence without associating a physical location or sensation? How would your prayer change if you consciously affirmed that God is not a body or form?
?
The passage denies any likeness to God. What mental images or concepts of God have you unconsciously formed that might contradict this? Are you ready to let go of them and worship Him as He truly is, beyond your imagination?

Divine Justice and Decree
Lists impossibilities related to divine justice and decree.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God is perfectly just and that all actions of creation occur by His decree, will, and creation.

Core Idea
God's decree is all wisdom and justice; nothing happens outside His will.

The final set of impossibilities deals with God's actions and His relationship to creation. Imam Ghazali declares that injustice is impossible for God, and that every action of His creatures occurs by His decree and will. This lesson establishes the foundation of predestination (qadar) within the framework of divine justice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and translation, focusing on the two Quranic verses quoted.
The verses serve as proof for the statements.
2
Identify the two key affirmations
First, injustice is impossible for God; His decree is wisdom and justice. Second, every action of creatures happens by His decree, creation, and will.
These affirm God's justice and omnipotence.
3
Analyze the Quranic evidence
The first verse (6:115) states God's word is truth and justice. The second (16:93) affirms that God guides and leads astray whom He wills.
These verses support the assertion that all actions are under God's control.
4
Reflect on divine justice and qadar
Consider how God's justice is compatible with His decree of all actions, including guidance and misguidance.
This is a deep theological topic; the passage affirms both without contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما ما يعتقد استحالته ، فهو : أن تعتقد أنه تعالى يستحيل عليه الحدوث ، والعدم ، بل هو تعالى بصفاته وأسمائه ، قديم باق ، دائم الوجود ، قائم على كل نفس بما كسبت ، ليس له أول ولا آخر ، بل هو الأول والآخر ، وأنه لا إله سواه ، لو كان فيهما آلهة إلا الله لفسدتا ، وأنه مستغن عن جميع خلقه ، غير محتاج الى ظهير في ملكه ، وأنه لا يشغله شأن عن شأن في قضائه وأمره ، وأنه لا يحويه مكان في سمواته ولا أرضه ، بل هو كما كان قبل خلق المكان ، وأنه ليس بجوهر ولا جسم ولا على صورة ولا شكل ، ولا له شبيه ولا مثل ، بل هو الأحد الصمد الذي لم يلد ولم يولد ولم يكن له كفوا أحد ،
وأنه لا تحله الحوادث والتغيرات ، ولا تلحقه النقائض والآفات ، وأنه لا يليق به الظلم ، بل قضاؤه كله حكمة وعدل ، وأنه ليس شيء من أفعال خليقته بغير قضائه وخلقه وارادته ، بل :

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that human actions are independent of God's will or that God could be unjust.
Correction: God is perfectly just, and all actions occur by His decree and will.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is true about God's decree?
A) It is sometimes unjust
B) It is all wisdom and justice
C) It changes over time
D) It applies only to some actions

Key Takeaway
God is perfectly just, and every action in creation occurs by His decree, will, and creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a painful trial, do you truly believe it is part of God's wise and just decree, or do you secretly doubt His justice? What would change if you fully embraced that this trial is 'all wisdom and justice'?
?
How does knowing that even your small sins occur by God's decree and will affect your repentance and reliance on His guidance? Are you willing to surrender your plans to His will, even when you don't understand?
?
Look at someone you know who is far from guidance. Does the verse 'He leads astray whom He wills' humble you or make you judgmental? How can you actively seek to be among those He guides?

Divine Attributes
beginner
4 min
The Obligatory Beliefs: God's Attributes of Knowledge, Will, and Perception
First section enumerates obligatory beliefs about God's attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the six obligatory beliefs about God's attributes as enumerated by Imam al-Ghazali.

Core Idea
God's attributes are unlike any created thing, yet they are real and obligatory to affirm.

In this foundational passage, Imam al-Ghazali presents the core attributes of God that every Muslim must believe. He moves from God's all-encompassing knowledge to His universal will, then to His attributes of hearing, seeing, and speech—always emphasizing their transcendence. This lesson unpacks each attribute and the underlying principle of divine incomparability.

Guided Path
1
Read the entire passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's rhythm and the Quranic verse at the end sink in.
Notice how the passage begins with knowledge and ends with the Quranic proof.
2
Identify each attribute
The passage mentions knowledge (implied by 'nothing hidden'), will (willer of every being), hearing, seeing, and speech. List them and note the negation of organs.
The phrase 'without an organ or instrument' applies to hearing, seeing, and speech.
3
Understand the principle of dissimilarity
The passage explicitly says God's attributes do not resemble attributes, just as His essence does not resemble essences. This is a core theological safeguard.
The Quranic verse 'There is nothing like unto Him' reinforces this.
4
Reflect on the obligatory nature
The passage ends with 'this is what is believed as obligatory.' Consider why these specific beliefs are considered essential for every Muslim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عنه مثقال ذرة في السموات ولا في الأرض ، وأنه مريد لكل كائن من خير أو شر ، ما شاء كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن ، وأنه سميع بصير ، متكلم بغير جارحة ولا آلة ، بل سمعه وبصره وكلامه صفات له ، لا تشبه صفاته الصفات ، كما لا تشبه ذاته الذوات ليس كمثله شيء وهو السميع البصير هذا ما يعتقد وجوبه
Not even the weight of a speck in the heavens nor in the earth is hidden from Him. He is the Willer of every being, good or evil; what He wills is, and what He does not will is not. He is Hearing, Seeing, Speaking without an organ or instrument; rather His Hearing, His Sight, and His Speech are attributes of Him. His attributes do not resemble attributes, just as His essence does not resemble essences. 'There is nothing like unto Him, and He is the Hearing, the Seeing.' This is what is believed as obligatory.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of the obligatory beliefs concerning God's attributes. It begins by affirming God's comprehensive knowledge: nothing escapes Him, not even the weight of a speck. Then it affirms His universal will: everything that occurs, whether good or evil, is by His will; nothing happens outside His volition. Next, it affirms His attributes of hearing, seeing, and speech, stressing that these are without body parts or instruments. The passage emphasizes that God's attributes are not like created attributes, just as His essence is not like created essences. It quotes the Quranic verse 'There is nothing like unto Him, and He is the Hearing, the Seeing' (Quran 42:11) as proof. The passage concludes by stating that this set of beliefs constitutes the obligatory creed.

Key Terms
وجوب
صفات
إرادة
سمع
بصر
كلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God's attributes are either identical to His essence or separate from it, or that they resemble human attributes.
Correction: The passage affirms that God's attributes are real and belong to Him, but they are utterly unlike any created attributes, just as His essence is unlike created essences.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT included in the obligatory beliefs about God?
A) He knows the weight of a speck in the heavens and earth.
B) He wills both good and evil.
C) He hears and sees without bodily organs.
D) He has a body like human bodies.

Key Takeaway
The obligatory beliefs about God's attributes include His all-encompassing knowledge, universal will, hearing, seeing, and speech without organs, all of which are unlike any created attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just read that God's will encompasses everything, including evil that happens in your life. Think of a recent hardship you faced. Do you truly believe it came from God's will, or do you hold a subtle resentment? Can you accept that what He wills is, and what He does not will is not, and surrender your heart to that in that specific situation? This week, when you recall that hardship, pause and say 'ما شاء كان' to affirm His will.
?
The passage says God hears and sees without an organ. He knows even the weight of a speck. Consider the last time you committed a sin in private, thinking no one sees. Do you really live with the conviction that His sight is always upon you, not as a surveillance but as a relationship? What would change in your behavior tonight if you truly believed that the One who sees without an eye is watching your every move?
?
The passage affirms God's speech without an organ. When you read the Quran, do you receive it as speech directly from the One who speaks without a mouth? Or do you treat it merely as a historical text? This week, before you open the Quran, remind yourself: 'He is the Speaking without an organ,' and listen for His address to you.

The Shahada and the Three Aspects of Oneness
Introduces the Shahada and the three dimensions of God's oneness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Shahada affirms God's oneness in three distinct aspects: kingdom, essence, and divinity.

Core Idea
The Shahada declares God's oneness in three ways: no partner, no equal, no rival.

Before exploring the divisions of tawheed, we must first grasp what the Shahada itself affirms. It does not merely state that God exists; it declares His absolute oneness in every sense—His actions, His essence, and His right to be worshipped. This passage introduces the threefold oneness that forms the foundation of Islamic faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to get an overview of the Shahada and the three aspects of oneness.
2
Identify the three aspects
Find the three 'waahid' statements and note how each differs: no partner (kingdom), no equal (essence), no rival (divinity).
The three aspects cover all dimensions of tawheed.
3
Reflect on the Shahada
Consider why the Shahada is the first pillar of Islam and how it encapsulates all three aspects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفهم طبيعة الرسالة والرسل على هذا النحو من الوساطة ، يسلمنا الى الحديث عن التوحيد الذي تقرره القاعدة الأولى التي نحن بصدد الحديث عنها وهي : أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله ، وأشهد أن محمدا رسول الله والذي سمى دين الاسلام من أجلها توحيدا، لأن مبناه على أن الله تعالى واحد في ملكه وأفعاله، لا شريك له، وواحد في ذاته وصفاته لانظير له، وواحد في الهيته وعبادته لا ند له والى هذه الأنواع الثلاثة ينقسم توحيد الأنبياء والمرسلين الذين جاؤ وا به من عند الله سبحانه، وهى متلازمة، كل نوع منها لا ينفك عن الآخر، فمن أتى بنوع منها ولم يأت بالآخر، فما ذاك إلا لأنه لم يأت به على وجه الكمال المطلوب والتوحيد : الذي تقرره وقررته القاعدة الأولى وهي : أشهد أن لا اله إلا الله وأشهد أن محمدا رسول الله نوعان : توحيد في المعرفة والاثبات : وهو توحيد الربوبية والأسماء والصفات وتوحيد في الطلب والمقصد : وهو توحيد الالهية والعبادة والنوع الاول : توحيد الربوبية والملك، وهو الاقرار بأن الله تعالى رب كل شيء ومالكه، وخالقه ورازقه، وأنه المحيي المميت، النافع الضار، المتفرد باجابة الدعاء عند الاضطرار، الذي له الأمر كله، وبيده الخير كله، القادر على ما يشاء، ليس له في ذلك شريك، ويدخل في ذلك الايمان بالقدر وهذا التوحيد لا يكفى العبد في حصول الاسلام، بل لابد أن يأتى مع ذلك
And this understanding of the nature of the message and the messengers as this kind of mediation leads us to talk about tawheed established by the first pillar which we are discussing, and it is: I bear witness that there is no god but Allah, and I bear witness that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah. And for this reason the religion of Islam was named tawheed, because its foundation is that Allah Almighty is one in His kingdom and actions, having no partner; and one in His essence and attributes, having no equal; and one in His divinity and worship, having no rival. And into these three types is divided the tawheed of the prophets and messengers who brought it from Allah, and they are inseparable, each type not being separate from the other. So whoever brings one type but not the other, then that is only because he did not bring it in the required perfect manner. And tawheed: that which the first pillar establishes and has established, namely 'I bear witness that there is no god but Allah and I bear witness that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' is of two types: Tawheed in knowledge and affirmation: which is tawheed of lordship (rububiyyah) and names and attributes; and tawheed in intention and purpose: which is tawheed of divinity (uluhiyyah) and worship. And the first type: tawheed of lordship and sovereignty, which is the acknowledgment that Allah is the Lord and Owner of everything, its Creator and Provider, and that He is the Giver of life and death, the Benefiter and Harmer, the Sole Responder to the supplication of the distressed, to Whom belongs all command, in Whose hand is all good, Powerful over whatever He wills, having no partner in that, and it includes belief in divine decree (qadar). And this tawheed is not sufficient for the servant in attaining Islam; rather he must also bring along with that [the second type].
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of tawheed as derived from the Shahada (the first pillar). It begins by stating that the correct understanding of prophethood leads to discussion of tawheed. The Shahada is presented: 'I bear witness that there is no god but Allah, and I bear witness that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah.' Islam is called 'tawheed' because it is founded on the oneness of God in three aspects: (1) oneness in His kingdom and actions (no partner), (2) oneness in His essence and attributes (no equal), and (3) oneness in His divinity and worship (no rival). These three types are inseparable; any incomplete manifestation is deficient. Then the passage makes a two-fold division based directly on the Shahada: (1) Tawheed of knowledge and affirmation, which encompasses lordship (rububiyyah) and names and attributes; (2) Tawheed of intention and purpose, which encompasses divinity (uluhiyyah) and worship. The first type is elaborated in detail: acknowledging Allah as Lord, Owner, Creator, Provider, Giver of life and death, Benefiter and Harmer, the only One who answers distressed supplications, the One with all command and good, the All-Powerful, without partner. This also includes belief in qadar. Crucially, the passage states that this first type alone is not sufficient for Islam; the second type (tawheed of worship) must accompany it.

Key Terms
توحيد
شريك
نظير
ند

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Shahada only affirms God's existence, not His exclusive right to worship.
Correction: The Shahada affirms tawheed in three aspects: lordship, essence, and worship.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many aspects of oneness does the Shahada establish?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
The Shahada is the foundation of tawheed and affirms God's oneness in three inseparable dimensions: lordship, essence, and worship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you declare 'La ilaha illa Allah', do you truly feel in your heart that there is absolutely no partner, equal, or rival to Allah in any aspect of your life? Examine a recent situation where you might have acted as if something else had ultimate control.
?
Think of a moment when you were tempted to please someone else more than Allah. In that moment, was there a rival to His divinity in your intention? How can you train your heart to remove such rivals starting today?
?
You have just learned that Islam is called tawheed because of these three dimensions. Does your daily life reflect that your worship is directed only to the One who has no partner, no equal, no rival? What is one concrete change you will make this week to align your actions with this truth?

The Three Types of Tawheed Are Inseparable
Explains the three types of tawheed of prophets and their inseparability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the three aspects of tawheed are inseparable and must all be fulfilled for perfect tawheed.

Core Idea
True tawheed requires all three aspects together; lacking one makes it incomplete.

Having learned the three aspects of tawheed, we now discover that they are not optional or independent. The prophets brought all three together, and any deficiency in one means deficient tawheed. This passage emphasizes their inseparability.

Guided Path
1
Read the short passage
This is a concise statement about the three types of tawheed of the prophets.
2
Understand 'mutalazimah'
The word 'متلازمة' means inseparable; note that each type depends on the other.
3
Reflect on the consequence
Why would bringing one type without the other be incomplete? Consider the perfection required.
The passage says it is not brought in the required perfect manner.

The Two Categories of Tawheed and the Role of Worship
Divides tawheed into two types and details the first type while asserting its insufficiency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between tawheed of knowledge/affirmation and tawheed of intention/purpose, and understand why believing in God's lordship alone is not enough for Islam.

Core Idea
Tawheed splits into knowing God as Lord and worshipping Him alone; the first without the second is incomplete.

Now we come to a crucial division: based on the Shahada, tawheed is of two types. The first, tawheed of lordship, might be easy to accept, but the passage warns that it alone does not bring one into Islam. The second type, tawheed of worship, is essential. This lesson explains the first type in detail and underscores the necessity of the second.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Focus on the two-part division and the details of the first type.
2
Identify the two types
Find where the text says 'نوعان' and note the names given.
3
Examine the first type
List the attributes mentioned under tawheed of lordship (rububiyyah).
4
Note the crucial statement
The last sentence explicitly says this type alone is insufficient; reflect on why.

Correction: The passage explicitly says this is insufficient; one must also worship Allah alone (tawheed of uluhiyyah).

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what must be added to tawheed of lordship for one to attain Islam?
A) Belief in prophets
B) Tawheed of worship
C) Belief in angels
D) Performing Hajj

Key Takeaway
Tawheed of lordship is necessary but not sufficient; true tawheed requires also tawheed of worship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You believe that Allah is the Sole Creator and Provider, but do you truly rely on Him alone when you face hardship, or do your actions betray a reliance on other means? What is one situation today where you can consciously turn to Him exclusively?
?
The passage clearly states that acknowledging God's lordship is not enough for salvation. Has your faith ever stopped at mere intellectual belief without translating into sincere worship? What would change if you took this statement literally?
?
If you were to examine your daily supplications, do you find yourself calling upon anyone other than Allah, even indirectly? How can you train yourself to direct every need, big or small, only to Him, trusting that He alone responds to the distressed?

Tawhid al-Asma' wa as-Sifat: Definition and Insufficiency
Ghazali defines the second type of Tawhid and asserts its insufficiency without the first type.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of Tawhid al-Asma' wa as-Sifat and why affirming Allah's names and attributes alone is not sufficient for Islam.

Core Idea
Affirming Allah's attributes is essential but not enough; worship of Allah alone is required.

Imam Ghazali now introduces the second type of Tawhid: the oneness of names and attributes. He lists many of Allah's beautiful names and lofty attributes, emphasizing that we must affirm them. However, he immediately warns that this alone does not secure one's Islam. The missing element is the first type: Tawhid al-Uluhiyyah, the oneness of worship. This lesson clarifies what this type entails and why it is incomplete by itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the list of attributes and the final statement about insufficiency.
The passage ends mid-sentence, but the key point is clear.
2
Identify the key attributes mentioned
Look at the attributes listed: knowledge, power, life, self-subsistence, will, wisdom, hearing, sight, kindness, mercy, being established over the Throne, etc. See how they describe Allah.
3
Focus on the crucial statement
Find the phrase 'wa hadha aydan la yakfi fi husul al-Islam' – this also is not sufficient for the attainment of Islam. Ask yourself why Ghazali would say that.
This is the main teaching point.
4
Reflect on the insufficiency
Consider that simply believing in God's attributes without worshipping Him alone is not enough. This shows the importance of Tawhid al-Uluhiyyah (the first type).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الثاني : توحيد الأسماء والصفات، وهو الاقرار بأن الله تعالى بكل شيء عليم ، وعلى كل شيء قدير ، وأنه الحي القيوم ، الذي لا تأخذه سنة ولا نوم ، له المشيئة النافذة ، والحكمة البالغة ، وأنه سميع بصير ، رؤوف رحيم ، على العرش استوى ، وعلى الملك احتوى ، وأنه الملك القدوس ، السلام المؤمن المهيمن ، العزيز الجبار المتكبر ، سبحان الله عما يشركون إلى غير ذلك الاسماء الحسنى ، والصفات العلى من وهذا أيضا لا يكفى في حصول الاسلام ، بل لابد مع ذلك من الاتيان
The second type: Tawhid of names and attributes. It is the affirmation that Allah the Exalted is Knower of everything, and over everything is Powerful, and that He is the Living, the Self-Sustaining, whom neither drowsiness nor sleep overtakes. His is the effective will and the perfect wisdom. And that He is Hearing, Seeing, Kind, Merciful. He is established above the Throne and encompasses the dominion. And that He is the King, the Holy, the Peace, the Faithful, the Guardian, the Mighty, the Compeller, the Supreme. Exalted is Allah above what they associate. And beyond that are the beautiful names and the lofty attributes. And this also is not sufficient for the attainment of Islam, rather along with that one must come...
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage defines the second category of Tawhid according to Imam Ghazali: Tawhid al-Asma' wa as-Sifat (Oneness of Names and Attributes). The author lists essential attributes that must be affirmed for Allah, such as absolute knowledge, power, life, self-subsistence, freedom from drowsiness and sleep, effective will, perfect wisdom, hearing, sight, kindness, mercy, being established over the Throne, encompassing dominion, and various names from the category of al-Asma' al-Husna like al-Malik, al-Quddus, etc. The listing is incomplete as it ends with a general reference to the rest of the beautiful names and lofty attributes. After this enumeration, Imam Ghazali makes a crucial theological point: merely affirming these attributes—even correctly—is not sufficient to enter Islam. One must also bring the first type, i.e., Tawhid al-Uluhiyyah (the oneness of worship). The phrase 'bil lā budda maʿa dhālika min al-ityān' is cut off, but the intended meaning is that one must come with the first type or with the full Tawhid. This guards against the error of those who might think that correct creedal affirmation of God's attributes (without tahrif, ta'til, etc.) is enough, while neglecting the active worship of Allah alone.

الاسماء الحسنى
الصفات العلى
لا يكفي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that if they affirm Allah's attributes correctly (without distortion or denial), they are guaranteed salvation.
Correction: Ghazali explicitly states that this type alone is not sufficient; one must also practice Tawhid al-Uluhiyyah—worshipping Allah alone without partners.

B) It is not sufficient for the attainment of Islam.
C) It is the same as Tawhid al-Uluhiyyah.
D) It is only for scholars.

Key Takeaway
Affirming Allah's names and attributes is necessary but not sufficient; true Islam requires also the oneness of worship.

?
In what areas of your life have you been content with 'knowing' about Allah without actually serving Him as the sole object of your devotion? Will you change that starting now?

Tawheed of Names and Attributes and Its Limits
Defines Tawheed al-Asma wa al-Sifat and states it is insufficient for Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of Tawheed of Names and Attributes, its insufficiency for Islam without Tawheed of Worship, and the historical example of the mushrikeen's rejection of ar-Rahman.

Core Idea
Affirming Allah's attributes is not enough; you must also worship Him alone.

This lesson covers the second category of tawheed: Tawheed of Names and Attributes. Imam al-Ghazali lists many divine names and attributes from the Quran, then makes a crucial point: the pagan Arabs also affirmed most of these attributes, yet they were not Muslims. This shows that correct belief about Allah's attributes must be accompanied by exclusive worship of Him.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Notice the list of attributes and the author's conclusion.
2
Identify the attributes and the conclusion
List the divine names and attributes mentioned. Then note the sentence: 'Yet this alone is not sufficient for attaining Islam.' Understand why.
The mushrikeen affirmed many attributes but still committed shirk.
3
Analyze the historical example
Focus on the rejection of the name ar-Rahman. Why did they reject it? What does this teach about the relationship between belief in attributes and worship?
Their rejection was obstinate, not ignorant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الثاني : توحيد الأسماء والصفات، وهو الاقرار بأن الله تعالى بكل شيء عليم ، وعلى كل شيء قدير ، وأنه الحي القيوم ، الذي لا تأخذه سنة ولا نوم ، له المشيئة النافذة ، والحكمة البالغة ، وأنه سميع بصير ، رؤوف رحيم ، على العرش استوى ، وعلى الملك احتوى ، وأنه الملك القدوس ، السلام المؤمن المهيمن ، العزيز الجبار المتكبر ، سبحان الله عما يشركون إلى غير ذلك الاسماء الحسنى ، والصفات العلى . وهذا أيضا لا يكفى في حصول الاسلام ، بل لابد مع ذلك من الاتيان بلازمه ، من توحيد الربوبية والالهية ، والكفار يقرون بجنس هذا النوع ، وان كان بعضهم قد ينكر بعض ذلك ، جهلا وعنادا ، كما قالوا : لا نعرف الرحمن الا رحمن اليمامة ، فأنزل الله إليهم : ﴿ وَهُمْ يَكْفُرُونَ بالرَّحْمَن )) . ويعلق الامام الحافظ ابن كثير فيقول : والظاهر أن انكارهم هذا إنما هو جحود وعناد وتعنت في كفرهم . ولم يعرف عنهم إنكار شيء من هذا التوحيد ، إلا في اسم الرحمن خاصة ، ولو كانوا ينكرونه لردوا على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، ذلك ، كما ردوا عليه توحيد الالهية ، فقالوا إجعل الآلهة إلها واحدا ، إن هذا لشيء عجاب . لا سيما السورة المكية مملؤة بهذا التوحيد .
The second type: Tawheed of Names and Attributes. It is the affirmation that Allah Almighty is Knower of all things, Powerful over all things, and that He is al-Hayy (the Ever-Living), al-Qayyum (the Self-Subsisting), Whom no slumber nor sleep overtakes; to Him belongs the effective will and perfect wisdom; He is All-Hearing, All-Seeing, Kind, Merciful; He is established over the Throne and encompasses the dominion; He is al-Malik (the King), al-Quddus (the Holy), as-Salam (the Source of Peace), al-Mu'min (the Giver of Security), al-Muhaymin (the Guardian), al-Aziz (the Almighty), al-Jabbar (the Compeller), al-Mutakabbir (the Supreme); glorified is Allah above what they associate. And to Him belong the beautiful names and lofty attributes. Yet this alone is not sufficient for attaining Islam; rather, one must also bring what is necessary for it, namely Tawheed of Lordship and Tawheed of Worship. The disbelievers affirm this type in general, although some of them may deny some of it out of ignorance and stubbornness, as when they said: 'We do not know ar-Rahman except the Rahman of Yamamah.' So Allah revealed to them: 'And they disbelieve in ar-Rahman.' Imam al-Hafiz Ibn Kathir comments: 'It seems that their denial was but obstinacy, stubbornness, and willfulness in their disbelief.' It is not known that they denied any of this tawheed except the name ar-Rahman specifically. Had they denied it, they would have rejected it upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) as they rejected Tawheed of Worship, saying: 'Has he made the gods one God? Indeed, this is a strange thing.' Especially the Meccan surahs are filled with this tawheed.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage defines the second category of tawheed according to later categorization: 'Tawheed of Names and Attributes' (al-Asma wa al-Sifat). The author lists various divine names and attributes — knowledge, power, life, self-subsistence, will, wisdom, hearing, sight, mercy, establishment over the Throne, encompassing dominion, and the specific names from the Quran: al-Malik, al-Quddus, etc. He emphasizes that affirming these attributes is essential but not sufficient for entering Islam. One must also bring the necessary concomitant: tawheed of lordship (rububiyyah) and tawheed of worship (uluhiyyah). The author then notes that the pre-Islamic Arabs generally affirmed God's attributes except the name ar-Rahman, which some rejected out of ignorance or obstinacy, as they recognized only a local deity called 'Rahman of Yamamah' (a false prophet). Allah responded by condemning their disbelief in ar-Rahman. Ibn Kathir clarifies that their denial was sheer stubbornness, not genuine ignorance. The passage further argues that had the Arabs denied other names/attributes, they would have contested the Prophet about them as they contested tawheed of worship. However, they did not widely deny other attributes except ar-Rahman. The Meccan surahs are filled with this tawheed of names and attributes. Thus the lesson: affirming Allah's attributes is not enough; one must also worship Him alone.

الرحمن
ابن كثير
الربوبية
الإلهية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Believing that simply affirming Allah's attributes (e.g., that He is All-Knowing) makes one a Muslim.
Correction: The passage shows that the mushrikeen also affirmed many attributes but were not Muslims because they committed shirk in worship. True Islam requires both correct belief about Allah and exclusive worship of Him.

Checkpoint

B) They were afraid of the Prophet

Key Takeaway
Tawheed of Names and Attributes, while necessary, is not sufficient for Islam; it must be accompanied by Tawheed of Worship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

What is one attribute of Allah that you have been hesitant to fully embrace? Today, the example of the mushrikeen shows that even denying one name (ar-Rahman) out of stubbornness is dangerous. Is there any name or attribute you resist, and what would change if you fully submitted to it?
?
The passage states that Tawheed of Names and Attributes must be accompanied by Tawheed of Worship. Commit to one act of worship today that you will do solely for Allah, without any shadow of showing off or seeking people's praise.

Definition and Foundation of Tawhid al-Uluhiyya
Imam al-Ghazali defines Tawhid al-Uluhiyya with its foundation, Quranic support, and ultimate significance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Tawhid al-Uluhiyya is built on sincere devotion to Allah in all inner and outer acts of worship, as defined by Imam al-Ghazali and supported by Quranic verses.

Core Idea
Worshipping Allah alone with love, fear, and hope is the essence of Tawhid.

Imam al-Ghazali begins by defining the foundation of Tawhid al-Uluhiyya: exclusive devotion to Allah in all acts of worship, both inward and outward. He then supports this with multiple Quranic verses and explains that this tawhid is the central purpose of creation and revelation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the foundation
Read the first sentence carefully. It states that Tawhid al-Uluhiyya is built on sincere devotion (ikhlas) in inner acts like love, fear, hope, trust, etc. This is the core meaning.
Notice that these are inner acts of worship.
2
See how it extends to all worship
The passage says this foundation leads to sincerity in all acts of worship, both apparent and hidden, with no partners.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
The author cites several verses that combine worship and reliance on Allah alone. Read each verse and see how they reinforce exclusive devotion.
4
Reflect on the significance
The passage concludes that this tawhid is the first and last of the religion, the criterion of faith, and the purpose of creation. Consider why it is so central.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتوحيد الالهية مبنى على إخلاص التأله الله تعالى من المحبة ، والخوف والرجاء ، والتوكل ، والرغبة ، والرهبة ، والدعاء الله وحده : وينبني على ذلك إخلاص العبادات كلها ظاهرها وباطنها الله وحده لا شريك له ، لا يجعل فيها شيئا لغيره ، لا لملك مقرب ، ولا لنبي مرسل ، فضلا عن غيرهما وهذا التوحيد هو الذي تضمنه قوله تعالى: ﴿ إِيَّاكَ نَعْبُدُ وَإِيَّاكَ نَسْتَعِينُ ﴾ وقوله تعالى : ﴿فَاعْبُدْهُ وَتَوَكَّل عَلَيْهِ وَمَا رَبُّكَ بِغَافِلٍ عَمَّا تَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ وقوله سبحانه : ( فَإِن تَوَلُّوا فَقُلْ حَسْيَ اللهُ لا إلهَ إِلا هُوَ عَلَيْهِ تَوَكَّلْتُ وَهُوَ رَبُّ الْعَرْشِ الْعَظِيم ) . وقوله تعالى : ﴿ رَّبُّ السَّمَوَاتِ والأَرض وَمَا بَيْنَهُمَا فَأَعْبُدْهُ وَاصْطَبِرٍ لِعِبَادَتِهِ هَلْ تَعلَمُ لَهُ سَمِيًّا ﴾ . وقوله سبحانه : ﴿ عَلَيْهِ تَوَكَّلْتُ وَإِلَيْهِ أُنِيبُ ﴾ وقوله تعالى : ( وَتَوَكَّل عَلَى الحَيِّ الَّذِي لَا يَمُوتُ وَسَبِّحْ بِحَمْدِهِ وَكَفَى بِهِ بِذُنُوب عِبَادِهِ خَبيراً ) وقوله سبحانه: ﴿ وَأعْبُدْ رَبَّكَ حَتَّى يَأْتِيَكَ اليَقِينُ ﴾ وهذا التوحيد هو أول الدين وآخره ، وباطنه وظاهره ، وهو أول دعوة الرسل و آخرها ، وهو معنى قول : لا إله إلا الله فإن إلاله هو المألوه المعبود بالمحبة ، والخشية ، والاجلال والتعظيم ، وجميع أنواع العبادة ، ولأجل هذا التوحيد ، خلقت الخليقة ، وأرسلت الرسل ، وأنزلت الكتب ، وبه افترق الناس إلى مؤمنين ، وكفار ، وسعداء أهل الجنة ، وأشقياء أهل النار ، قال تعالى : يَا أَيُّهَا النَّاسُ اعْبُدُوا رَبَّكُمُ الَّذِى خَلَقَكُمْ وَالَّذِينَ مِن قَبْلِكُمْ لَعَلَّكُمْ تَتَّقُونَ
And Tawhid al-Uluhiyya is founded on sincere devotion to Allah from love, fear, hope, trust, desire, awe, and supplication to Allah alone. And upon that is built sincerity in all acts of worship, both apparent and inward, for Allah alone without any partner; nothing is to be associated with Him in them, neither a close angel nor a sent prophet, let alone others. This is the tawhid which is contained in His saying, the Exalted: "You alone we worship and You alone we ask for help" (al-Fatiha 5); and His saying, the Exalted: "So worship Him and rely upon Him. And your Lord is not unaware of what you do" (Hud 123); and His saying, Glorified: "But if they turn away, say: Sufficient for me is Allah; there is no deity except Him. I rely upon Him, and He is the Lord of the Great Throne" (at-Tawbah 129); and His saying, the Exalted: "Lord of the heavens and the earth and whatever is between them, so worship Him and be patient in His worship. Do you know of any likeness to Him?" (Maryam 65); and His saying, Glorified: "Upon Him I rely and to Him I turn" (Hud 88); and His saying, the Exalted: "And rely upon the Immortal who does not die, and exalt [Him] with His praise. And sufficient is He to be acquainted with the sins of His servants" (al-Furqan 58); and His saying, Glorified: "And worship your Lord until there comes to you the certainty [death]" (al-Hijr 99). This tawhid is the first of the religion and its last, its inward and its outward, it is the first call of the messengers and their last, and it is the meaning of the statement: There is no deity except Allah — for al-Ilah is the object of worship, worshipped with love, fear, veneration, and exaltation, and all types of worship. And for the sake of this tawhid, creation was created, messengers were sent, and scriptures were revealed; and by it people are divided into believers and disbelievers, fortunate inhabitants of Paradise and wretched inhabitants of Hellfire. He, the Exalted, said: "O mankind, worship your Lord who created you and those before you, that you may become righteous" (al-Baqarah 21).
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage defines and explains Tawhid al-Uluhiyya, the oneness of Allah in worship. The author begins by stating its foundation: sincerity (ikhlas) in directing all acts of devotion to Allah alone. These acts include love (mahabbah), fear (khawf), hope (raja'), trust (tawakkul), desire (raghbah), awe (rahbah), and supplication (du'a'). Upon this foundation, the author explains, is built sincerity in all acts of worship, both outward (like prayer and fasting) and inward (like intention and reliance). No partner is to be associated in any of these acts, whether that partner be an angel, a prophet, or any other being. The author then supports this with several Quranic verses that combine worship and reliance on Allah alone: Surah al-Fatiha (5), Surah Hud (123), Surah at-Tawbah (129), Surah Maryam (65), Surah Hud (88), Surah al-Furqan (58), and Surah al-Hijr (99). He then emphasizes that this tawhid is the first and last of the religion, its inward and outward, and the first and last call of all messengers. It is the meaning of "La ilaha illa Allah" (there is no deity except Allah), elaborating that al-Ilah is the One who is worshipped with love, fear, veneration, and all kinds of worship. The purpose of creation, prophethood, and scripture is this tawhid; it is the criterion that divides people into believers and disbelievers, and ultimately into the people of Paradise and Hellfire. The passage concludes with Surah al-Baqarah (21), commanding worship of the Creator.

Correction: The passage shows that Tawhid al-Uluhiyya is founded on sincere devotion in inner acts like love and fear, and extends to all acts of worship, with no partners.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

If it is that central, why do you often treat it as a mere abstract belief rather than the living reality that drives every action you take? The 28 Beliefs Under Self-Sufficiency (Istighna)
The author enumerates the 28 beliefs derived from the attribute of divine self-sufficiency (istighna).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the 28 beliefs that follow from Allah's self-sufficiency (istighna) and how they encompass essential attributes, active attributes, and necessary negations.

Core Idea
Divine self-sufficiency (istighna) entails 28 distinct beliefs, not just a few.

In this passage, Imam al-Ghazali enumerates the 28 beliefs that are logically entailed by the divine attribute of self-sufficiency (istighna). This list is not arbitrary; it systematically derives from what it means for Allah to be independent of all else. The beliefs include essential attributes, the attributes of hearing, sight, and speech, and necessary negations such as freedom from purpose and obligation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to grasp the overall enumeration.
Note the unclear words; they will be clarified in the commentary.
2
Identify the categories
Break the list into groups: essential attributes (5), necessity of hearing/sight/speech (3), their concomitants (3), negations (3), and their opposites.
The total count of 28 includes the opposites of each attribute mentioned.
3
Reflect on the logic
Ask why each category is necessary for self-sufficiency. For example, if Allah is self-sufficient, He must be pre-eternal and not dependent on anything.
This shows the systematic nature of kalam reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فدخل تحت الاستغناء ثمانية وعشرون عقيدة : الوجود، والقدم، والبقاء والمخالفة للحوادث والقيام بالنفس . ووجوب السمع له ، والبصر والكلام ، ولوازمها وهي : يكوينه سميعاً بصيراً ، متكلما ، وتنزهه عن الغرض في أفعاله وأحكامه ، وعن وجوب شيء عليه فعلا ونزكا ، وعن كون شيء من أودعها الله فيه ، وأضدادها ، فجملتها ثمانية وعشرون عقيدة
So under self-sufficiency (istighna) there enter twenty-eight beliefs: existence, pre-eternity, everlastingness, dissimilarity to created things, self-subsistence, and the necessity of hearing, sight, and speech for Him, and their necessary concomitants, which are: His being hearing, seeing, speaking, and His transcendence above purpose in His actions and judgments, and above any obligation upon Him in action or leaving, and above anything being from what Allah has placed in it, and their opposites. So their total is twenty-eight beliefs.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of the 28 beliefs that fall under the concept of divine self-sufficiency (istighna). The author lists the necessary attributes of Allah that demonstrate His complete independence from all else. These include the essential attributes (existence, pre-eternity, everlastingness, dissimilarity to creation, self-subsistence), the attributes of hearing, sight, and speech and their necessary implications, and then negations—that Allah is free from purpose in His actions, from any obligation upon Him, and from any dependence on created things. The opposites of these are also included. The enumeration is systematic, showing how each attribute implies a belief.

الوجود
القدم
البقاء
المخالفة للحوادث
القيام بالنفس
سميع
بصير
متكلم
التنزه عن الغرض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Divine self-sufficiency only implies a few attributes.
Correction: This list shows it encompasses 28 distinct beliefs, including essential attributes, active attributes, and necessary negations.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT among the 28 beliefs under istighna?
A) Existence
B) Omnipotence
C) Pre-eternity
D) Self-subsistence

Key Takeaway
Divine self-sufficiency (istighna) implies 28 beliefs covering essential attributes, active attributes, and necessary negations, demonstrating Allah's complete independence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live with the awareness that Allah is self-sufficient and independent of your actions? How would your worship change if you sincerely believed that your obedience adds nothing to His perfection and your disobedience detracts nothing from His majesty?
?
When you consider that Allah has no purpose (gharad) in His actions and judgments, how does that challenge the way you question His decrees? Will you submit to His will without demanding to know the 'why' behind trials and blessings?
?
Reflect on the belief that Allah is not obligated to do anything for you. If He gave you nothing, He would not be unjust. How does this deepen your gratitude for every breath and every blessing you have? Will you thank Him today with a heart that acknowledges His absolute independence and your complete dependence?

Divine Attributes
beginner
4 min
The Beginner and the Doer of His Will
Commentary on the first two divine attributes from the opening hamdalah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meanings of Allah's attributes 'al-Mubdi'' (the Beginner) and 'al-Fa''al lima yurid' (the Doer of whatever He wills) as explained by Imam al-Ghazali.

Core Idea
Allah originates creation and restores it, and nothing prevents Him from doing whatever He wills.

Imam al-Ghazali opens his Qawa'id al-'Aqa'id with praise of Allah, highlighting two key attributes: His power to begin and restore creation, and His absolute freedom in action. The commentator explains these attributes, emphasizing that Allah's actions are unconstrained and His will is always executed.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the original text and its literal translation to absorb the commentator's language.
2
Understand the first attribute: al-Mubdi' al-Mu'id
Note that Allah begins creation without a model and restores it after annihilation. This is a consensus among Muslims.
3
Understand the second attribute: al-Fa''al lima yurid
This affirms that nothing is impossible for Allah; He does as He wills without objection or hindrance.
The commentary gives examples of Paradise and Hell, and how He deals with the disobedient.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider how these attributes establish Allah's sovereignty and independence from all constraints.
This lesson sets the foundation for understanding divine power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مقدمة :
الحمد لله المبدىء المعيد (١) ، الفعال لما يريد (۲) ، ذي العرش المجيد (٣) والبطش الشديد (٤) ، الهادي صفوة العبيد ، الى المنهج الرشيد ، والمسلك السديد

(1) أجمع المسلمون على أن الله عز وجل ، هو المبدىء المفيد ، يبدأ الخلق ثم يعيده ، يبدأ الخلق بايجاده أولا على غير مثال سبق منه ، ويعيده بعد إفنائه إياه (۲) لا يمتنع عليه مراد من أفعاله وأفعال غيره ، فهو سبحانه يفعل ما يريد على ما يراه ، لا يعترض عليه أحد ، ولا يغلبه غالب فيدخل أولياءه الجنة لا يمنعه مانع ، ويدخل أعداءه النار لا ينصرهم منه ناصر ، ويمهل العصاة على ما يشاء الى أن يجازيهم ، ويعاجلهم بالعقوبة إذا شاء ، فهو يفعل ما يريد . (۳) أي خالقه ومالكه ، والعرش الجسم المحيط بسائر الاجسام ، سمي به لارتفاعه ، وقد ورد في الحديث الصحيح : ( ما السموات السبع والأرضون السبع في جنب الكرس الا كحلة ملقاة في أرض فلاة ، والكرس عند العرش » ويقول الراغب : عرش الله مما لا يعلمه البشر الا بالاسم والمجيد : يحتمل أن يكون صفة العرش ، ومجده علوه وعظمة ، أو صفة الله تعالى ، أي عظيم في ذاته وصفاته ، فإنه واجب الوجود قام بالقدرة والحكمة .
(٤) البطش : أخلا بعنف وصوله ، ومعنى شدة بطشه مضاعفة عنفه ، وهكذا فسر العلماء قوله تعالى : ( إن بطش ربك لشديد ) . وقد ورد تفسير البطش : بأنه سرعة الانتقام وعدم التؤدة في العفو ، وقوله تعالى : إن بطش ربك لشديد ) تنبيه على أنه سريع الانتقام
Introduction: Praise be to Allah, the Beginner and Restorer (1), the Doer of whatever He wills (2), the Possessor of the Glorious Throne (3) and the Severe in Seizure (4), the Guide of the chosen servants to the right path and the straight way.
(1) The Muslims are agreed that Allah, mighty and majestic, is the Beginner and Restorer: He begins creation then restores it. He begins creation by bringing it into existence first without any preceding model from Him, and He restores it after annihilating it. (2) Nothing He wills is impossible for Him from His own actions or the actions of others. So He, glorified, does whatever He wills as He sees fit. No one objects to Him, and no one overcomes Him. He enters His friends into Paradise with none to prevent, and He enters His enemies into the Fire with none to help them against Him. He gives respite to the disobedient as He wishes until He recompenses them, and He hastens punishment for them if He wills. So He does whatever He wills. (3) That is, its Creator and Owner. The Throne is the body that encompasses all other bodies; it is called thus for its height. It has been reported in the authentic hadith: 'The seven heavens and the seven earths in comparison to the Kursi are but like a ring thrown in a desert, and the Kursi in comparison to the Throne is like that.' And al-Raghib says: The Throne of Allah is something that humans cannot know except by name. 'Al-Majid': it is possible that it is an attribute of the Throne, its majesty being its height and greatness, or an attribute of Allah, meaning He is great in His essence and attributes, for He is the Necessary Existence, established by power and wisdom. (4) 'Al-Batsh': seizure with violence and force. The meaning of the severity of His seizure is the doubling of His force. Thus the scholars interpreted the saying of the Exalted: 'Indeed, the seizure of your Lord is severe.' And it has been reported that 'al-batsh' is interpreted as swift vengeance and lack of deliberation in pardon. And the saying of the Exalted: 'Indeed, the seizure of your Lord is severe' is a warning that He is swift in vengeance.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the opening invocation (hamdalah) of Ghazali's Qawaid al-Aqaid. It begins by quoting the original text: 'Praise be to Allah, the Beginner and Restorer, the Doer of whatever He wills, the Possessor of the Glorious Throne and the Severe in Seizure, the Guide of the chosen servants to the right path and the straight way.' Then each of the first four attributes is explained in sequence.

1. The first attribute, 'al-Mubdi' al-Mu'id' (the Beginner and Restorer), is defined: Allah originates creation without a prior model and then restores it after annihilation. This is a consensus among Muslims.

2. The second attribute, 'al-Fa''al lima yurid' (the Doer of whatever He wills), affirms Allah's absolute power over all actions—His own and others'. He is not subject to constraint: no one can object or overcome Him. He grants Paradise and Hell as He wills, and may delay or hasten punishment for the disobedient.

3. The third attribute, 'Dhi al-'Arsh al-Majid' (Possessor of the Glorious Throne), explains that 'arsh (throne) is a body encompassing all bodies, named for its height. A hadith is cited comparing the heavens and earth to the Kursi, and the Kursi to the Throne. The commentator also cites al-Raghib, noting that the reality of the Throne is known only by name. 'Al-Majid' may describe the Throne (its height and greatness) or Allah (His greatness in essence and attributes, being the Necessary Existent established by power and wisdom).

4. The fourth attribute, 'al-Batsh al-Shadid' (the Severe in Seizure), defines 'batsh' as violent seizure. The severity is the doubling of force. Scholars interpret this as swift vengeance and lack of hesitation in punishment, citing the Quranic verse 'Indeed, the seizure of your Lord is severe.' The commentator concludes that this warns of Allah's swift retribution.

Key Terms
المبدىء
المعيد
الفعال لما يريد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what does 'al-Mubdi' al-Mu'id' mean?
A) Allah creates and then destroys.
B) Allah begins creation and restores it after annihilation.
C) Allah gives life and death.
D) Allah is the First and the Last.

Key Takeaway
Allah is the sole originator and restorer of creation, and His will is absolutely unrestricted.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah is the Beginner of your existence, why do you often live as if you created and sustained yourself? How would your daily choices change if you truly acknowledged that He originates and restores everything, including your very life?
?
Allah does whatever He wills, and no one can overcome Him. In what area of your life are you resisting His will, acting as if you can prevent His decree? What would it look like to surrender that area fully today?
?
He gives respite to the disobedient as He wishes. Are you taking His patience as a license to delay repentance? When will you respond to His will for you to return before the respite ends?

The Glorious Throne and the Severe Seizure
Commentary on the attributes of the Throne and severe seizure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meanings of the attributes 'Dhi al-'Arsh al-Majid' (Possessor of the Glorious Throne) and 'al-Batsh al-Shadid' (the Severe in Seizure), including the nature of the Throne and the concept of divine vengeance.

Core Idea
The Throne is a created body encompassing all, and Allah's seizure is severe and swift.

The commentary continues with the third and fourth attributes from the hamdalah. First, it explains the Throne ('arsh) as a body that encompasses all other bodies, and discusses the attribute 'Majid' (Glorious) which can refer to the Throne or to Allah Himself. Then it defines 'batsh' (seizure) as violent force, and the severity as swift vengeance.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the passage covering the Throne and the seizure attribute.
2
Understand the nature of the Throne
Note that the Throne is a created body encompassing all bodies, and its reality is known only by name, as al-Raghib states.
The hadith compares the heavens and earth to a ring in a desert relative to the Kursi, and the Kursi to the Throne.
3
Interpret 'al-Majid'
The attribute 'Majid' may describe the Throne (its height and greatness) or Allah Himself (great in essence and attributes).
4
Understand 'al-Batsh al-Shadid'
It means violent seizure with intensity, interpreted as swift vengeance without hesitation in punishment.
The Quranic verse 'Indeed, the seizure of your Lord is severe' is cited.
5
Reflect on the implications
Consider how these attributes emphasize Allah's majesty and his power to punish swiftly.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may imagine the Throne as a literal seat where God sits, like a king on a throne.

The Attributes of Allah in the Opening Praise
Commentary explaining the meanings of God's attributes in the opening praise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meanings of the four divine attributes mentioned in the opening praise: al-Mubdi' al-Mu'id, al-Fa''al lima yurid, Dhu al-Arsh al-Majid, and al-Batsh al-Shadid.

Core Idea
Allah's attributes in the opening praise affirm His absolute power, creation, and justice.

This lesson explores the commentary on the opening praise of the book, where the author explains key divine attributes. Each attribute reveals a facet of Allah's sovereignty and action. By studying these explanations, we gain deeper insight into Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview. Notice the structure: praise followed by numbered explanations.
The passage is divided into four main sections, each corresponding to an attribute.
2
Understand 'al-Mubdi' al-Mu'id'
Focus on the first attribute: Allah as the Originator and Returner. Understand the consensus on His creating and returning creation.
3
Understand 'al-Fa''al lima yurid'
The second attribute emphasizes Allah's absolute freedom to do as He wills, with no hinderance.
4
Understand the Throne and Glory
The third attribute describes Allah as Owner of the Throne, the Glorious. Note the discussion on the meaning of 'al-arsh' and 'al-majid'.
The Throne is described as the body encompassing all bodies.
5
Understand 'al-Batsh al-Shadid'
The fourth attribute refers to Allah's severe seizure, interpreted as swift punishment. Note the conclusion that all acts are created by Allah.
The common misunderstanding is that this refers to physical violence; the commentary clarifies it is swift divine justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(1) أجمع المسلمون على أن الله عز وجل ، هو المبدىء المفيد ، يبدأ الخلق ثم يعيده ، يبدأ الخلق بايجاده أولا على غير مثال سبق منه ، ويعيده بعد إفنائه إياه (۲) لا يمتنع عليه مراد من أفعاله وأفعال غيره ، فهو سبحانه يفعل ما يريد على ما يراه ، لا يعترض عليه أحد ، ولا يغلبه غالب فيدخل أولياءه الجنة لا يمنعه مانع ، ويدخل أعداءه النار لا ينصرهم منه ناصر ، ويمهل العصاة على ما يشاء الى أن يجازيهم ، ويعاجلهم بالعقوبة إذا شاء ، فهو يفعل ما يريد . (۳) أي خالقه ومالكه ، والعرش الجسم المحيط بسائر الاجسام ، سمي به لارتفاعه ، وقد ورد في الحديث الصحيح : ( ما السموات السبع والأرضون السبع في جنب الكرس الا كحلة ملقاة في أرض فلاة ، والكرس عند العرش » ويقول الراغب : عرش الله مما لا يعلمه البشر الا بالاسم والمجيد : يحتمل أن يكون صفة العرش ، ومجده علوه وعظمة ، أو صفة الله تعالى ، أي عظيم في ذاته وصفاته ، فإنه واجب الوجود قام بالقدرة والحكمة . (٤) البطش : أخلا بعنف وصوله ، ومعنى شدة بطشه مضاعفة عنفه ، وهكذا فسر العلماء قوله تعالى : ( إن بطش ربك لشديد ) . وقد ورد تفسير البطش : بأنه سرعة الانتقام وعدم التؤدة في العفو ، وقوله تعالى : إن بطش ربك لشديد ) تنبيه على أنه سريع الانتقام
وفي هذه الجمل : إشارة الى أن جميع افعال العباد مخلوقة لله تعالى ، وانه تعالى لا يجب عليه شيء لأنها دالة على أنه يفعل ما يريد .
Introduction: Praise be to Allah, the Originator, the Returner (1), the Doer of what He wills (2), the Owner of the Throne, the Glorious (3) and of severe Seizure (4), the Guide of the elite of servants to the right path and the correct way. (1) The Muslims are agreed that Allah, Mighty and Majestic, is the Originator, the Benefactor; He begins creation then returns it; He begins creation by bringing it into existence first without any prior example from Him, and returns it after annihilating it. (2) No desired thing from His actions and the actions of others is impossible for Him; He, glorified, does what He wills as He sees fit; no one objects to Him, and no one overcomes Him; He enters His friends into Paradise with none to prevent, and enters His enemies into the Fire with none to help them; He delays the disobedient as He wishes until He recompenses them, and hastens punishment for them if He wills; thus He does what He wills. (3) Meaning its Creator and Owner; the Throne is the body encompassing all bodies, so named for its elevation. It has come in the authentic hadith: 'The seven heavens and the seven earths compared to the Footstool are but like a ring thrown in a vast desert, and the Footstool compared to the Throne is like that.' al-Raghib says: The Throne of Allah is something that humans know only by name. al-Majid: It is possible that it is a description of the Throne, its majesty being its height and greatness, or a description of Allah Almighty, i.e., great in His essence and attributes, for He is the Necessary Existence, established with power and wisdom. (4) al-Batsh: He seizes with violence and force; the meaning of the severity of His seizure is the doubling of His force. Thus the scholars have interpreted His statement: 'Indeed, the seizure of your Lord is severe.' It has been reported that the interpretation of al-Batsh is: swift revenge and lack of deliberation in forgiveness. His statement: 'Indeed, the seizure of your Lord is severe' is a warning that He is swift in revenge. And in these sentences: an indication that all acts of servants are created by Allah Almighty, and that He Almighty is not obliged to do anything because they indicate that He does what He wills.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the opening phrase of the book, elaborating on the divine attributes mentioned. The author first states the praise to Allah, then provides detailed explanations of each attribute. He begins with 'al-Mubdi' al-Mu'id' (the Originator and Returner), explaining that Allah creates and then brings back creation. He then explains 'al-Fa''al lima yurid' (the Doer of what He wills), emphasizing that nothing prevents Allah from doing what He wills. Next, he explains 'Dhu al-Arsh al-Majid' (Owner of the Throne, the Glorious), describing the Throne as a body encompassing all bodies and citing a hadith about its vastness. He mentions that 'al-Majid' could describe the Throne or Allah's greatness. Finally, he explains 'al-Batsh al-Shadid' (the Severe Seizure), interpreting it as swift vengeance and lack of delay in punishment. The passage concludes with a remark that all actions of servants are created by Allah and that He is not obliged to do anything, as indicated by these attributes.

Key Terms
المبدىء المعيد
الفعال لما يريد
ذي العرش المجيد
البطش الشديد
العرش
المجيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that 'al-Batsh al-Shadid' refers to physical violence by Allah.
Correction: The commentary explains that it means swift divine justice and punishment, not physical violence.

Checkpoint
What does the commentary say about the meaning of 'al-Mubdi' al-Mu'id'?
A) He creates and then abandons creation
B) He creates first and then returns creation after annihilating it
C) He creates only once
D) He only returns creation

Key Takeaway
The opening praise of the book highlights Allah's attributes of creation, absolute will, sovereignty, and swift justice, reaffirming His control over all actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that Allah does whatever He wills, and no one can object to Him. In your daily life, where do you find yourself resisting His will—through worry, pride, or disobedience? What would change if you truly believed nothing can overcome His plan?
?
The attribute of severe seizure (البطش الشديد) reminds you that Allah is swift in punishing the disobedient. Think of a sin you have been hiding or justifying. As you sit with this lesson, how does the reality of swift justice affect your heart? Will you repent right now, and what will you do to show sincerity?
?
Allah is the Originator and Returner: He brought you into existence and will bring you back. Does your life reflect this awareness, or do you live as if this world is permanent? Before you move on, commit to one concrete action today that prepares you for the return to your Lord.
