الإحاطة
السر
الهواجس
الخواطر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Allah does not know minor details or that His knowledge is acquired or partial.
Correction: The passage shows that Allah knows the most hidden things, like an ant on a rock at night, and that His knowledge encompasses all categories of things without exception.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what example is given to show Allah's knowledge of the most hidden things?
A) The movement of the sun and moon
B) The creeping of a black ant on a solid rock in the dark night
C) The thoughts of angels
D) The number of stars

Key Takeaway
Allah's knowledge is absolutely all-encompassing, covering even the most hidden and minuscule details.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If no ant on a dark rock is hidden from Allah, then surely no sin of yours is hidden either. Does this make you despair of His mercy, or does it drive you to sincere repentance? Be honest: which feeling is stronger, and why?
?
Allah knows what is in your mind before you even think it. So why do you still pretend before Him that your intentions are pure when they are not? What change must you make in your private moments to align your inner life with your outer claim of faith?

The Eternal and Unchanging Nature of Divine Knowledge
Ghazali affirms the eternal nature of divine knowledge and refutes views that suggest change.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's knowledge is eternal, not acquired, and that it does not involve any change or indwelling in His essence.

Core Idea
Allah's knowledge is eternal and not subject to any change or acquisition.

This passage addresses a crucial theological point: the nature of divine knowledge. Ghazali clarifies that Allah's knowledge is eternal (qadim) and not a new occurrence in His essence, refuting heretical views that imply change. The footnote names the groups that held erroneous beliefs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Note the key terms: 'قديم أزلي' (eternal, pre-eternal) and 'الحلول والانتقال' (indwelling and transmission).
The passage is short but dense.
2
Identify the affirmation
Find the statement that describes Allah's knowledge as eternal and pre-eternal, and that He has never ceased to be described with it.
This is the positive assertion.
3
Identify the negation
Find the negation: Allah does not know new things that occur in His essence by way of indwelling or transmission.
This refutes views that imply change.
4
Understand the refutation
Read footnote (3) to see which groups held the erroneous view: Jahm ibn Safwan and the Rafidah.
Jahm ibn Safwan founded the Jahmi sect, and the Rafidah are a branch of Shi'a.
5
Reflect on the importance
Ask yourself why it is necessary to affirm that Allah's knowledge is eternal and unchanging. Consider the implications for other divine attributes.
This maintains Allah's perfection and immutability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العلم (٤) :
وأنه عالم بجميع المعلومات (٥) ، محيط بما يجري من تخوم الارضين الى أعلى السموات (٦) وأنه عالم لا يعزب عن علمه مثقال ذرة في الأرض ولا في السماء ، بل يعلم دبيب النملة السوداء ، على الصخرة الصماء ، في الليلة الظلماء(۱) ويدرك حركة الذر في جو الهواء ، ويعلم السر وأخفى (۲) ، ويطلع على هواجس الضمائر وحركات الخواطر ، وخفيات السرائر ، بعلم قديم أزلي لم يزل موصوفاً به في أزل الأزال ، لا يعلم متجدد حاصل في ذاته بالحلول والانتقال (۳).
(٤) وهي الصفة الثانية من صفات المعاني ، وهو المتعلق بكل واجب ، وكل مستحيل ، وكل جائز ، وهو صفة أزلية لها تعلق بالشيء على وجه الإحاطة به على ما هو عليه دون سبق خفاء.
(٥) موجوداً كان ذلك المعلوم أو معدوما محالا كان أو ممكنا ، قديما كان أو حادثا ، متناهيا كان أو غير متناه ، جزئيا كان أو كليا ، مركبا كان أو بسيطا.
(٦) مصداقاً لقوله تعالى : ( وأن الله قد أحاط بكل شيء علما ) فعلمه أحاط بالمعلومات كلها ، فعلى هذا التأويل يكون المحيط من أوصافه الازلية ، لأنه لم يزل عالما بالمعلومات كلها ، ودليل هذه الإحاطة قوله تعالى : ﴿ وَمَا يَعْزُبُ عَنْ عِلمِهِ مِثقَالَ ذَرَّة في الأرض ولا في السموات ) .
(۱) وكيف وهو خالقها ألا يعلم من خلق وهو اللطيف الخبير ، وإيراد هذه الاوصاف تنبيها على كمال الدقة والخفاء.
(۲) يعلم السر ، وما أخفى من السر ، وهو ما يطرأ وجوده في ضمير صاحبه ، فيعلمه قبل أن يقع بخاطر صاحبه.
(۳) كما ذهب اليه جهم بن صفوان والرافضة .
Knowledge (4):
And that He is Knower of all known things (5), encompassing whatever occurs from the depths of the earths to the highest heavens (6), and that He is Knower from whose knowledge not the weight of a particle escapes in the earth nor in the heavens. Rather, He knows the creeping of the black ant on the solid rock in the dark night (1), and He perceives the movement of the motes in the air, and He knows the secret and what is more hidden (2), and He is informed of the inner thoughts of consciences, the movements of passing thoughts, and the hidden secrets of innermost hearts, with an eternal, pre-eternal knowledge with which He has never ceased to be described in the eternity of eternities. He does not know a new thing occurring in His essence by way of indwelling or transmission (3).
(4) It is the second attribute of the attributes of meanings. It relates to every obligatory, every impossible, and every possible thing. It is an eternal attribute that has a relation to a thing in the manner of encompassing it as it is, without prior concealment.
(5) Whether that known thing is existent or non-existent, impossible or possible, eternal or originated, finite or infinite, particular or universal, compound or simple.
(6) In confirmation of His statement: 'And Allah encompasses everything in knowledge.' So His knowledge encompasses all known things. According to this interpretation, 'the Encompasser' is among His eternal attributes, because He has never ceased to be Knower of all known things. And the proof of this encompassing is His statement: 'And not the weight of a particle escapes His knowledge in the earth nor in the heavens.'
(1) And how? He is their Creator. Does He not know whom He created, while He is the Subtle, the Aware? The mention of these descriptions is a notification of the perfection of precision and hiddenness.
(2) He knows the secret and what is more hidden than the secret. It is what comes into existence in the conscience of its owner; He knows it before it occurs to the thought of its owner.
(3) As is held by Jahm ibn Safwan and the Rafidah.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the divine attribute of knowledge (al-ʿilm). It begins by stating that Allah is the Knower of all known things, encompassing everything from the depths of the earths to the highest heavens. No particle escapes His knowledge. The passage then gives vivid examples: He knows the creeping of a black ant on a solid rock in the dark night, the movement of motes in the air, the secret and what is more hidden, and the inner thoughts of consciences and hidden secrets. This knowledge is described as eternal (qadīm azalī), with which Allah has never ceased to be described. Importantly, it is not a knowledge that is new or occurring in His essence by way of indwelling (ḥulūl) or transmission (intiqlāl), refuting the views of Jahm ibn Safwan and the Rafidah. The footnotes elaborate: (4) states that knowledge is the second attribute of meanings (ṣifāt al-maʿānī), relating to everything necessary (wājib), impossible (mustaḥīl), and possible (jāʾiz). It is an eternal attribute that encompasses the thing as it is without prior concealment. (5) specifies that this knowledge covers all categories: existent or non-existent, impossible or possible, eternal or originated, finite or infinite, particular or universal, compound or simple. (6) provides scriptural evidence from the Qur'an: 'And Allah encompasses everything in knowledge' (65:12) and 'Not the weight of a particle escapes His knowledge' (34:3). Footnotes (1) and (2) further clarify: (1) asks rhetorically how He could not know when He is the Creator, and notes that these descriptions highlight His perfect subtlety and awareness. (2) explains that He knows the secret and what is even more hidden, knowing it before it occurs to the thought of its owner. Thus, the passage affirms the absolute, eternal, and all-encompassing nature of Allah's knowledge.

صفات المعاني
الأزل
الحلول والانتقال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Allah's knowledge is acquired or changes over time, or that new events occur in His essence.
Correction: The passage affirms that Allah's knowledge is eternal and not subject to change, refuting the views of Jahm ibn Safwan and the Rafidah who claimed indwelling or transmission.

Checkpoint
Which groups are mentioned in footnote (3) as holding the incorrect view about Allah's knowledge?
A) The Mu'tazila and the Khawarij
B) Jahm ibn Safwan and the Rafidah
C) The Ash'aris and the Maturidis
D) The philosophers and the Sufis

Key Takeaway
Allah's knowledge is eternal and immutable; it does not involve any change or acquisition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever secretly thought that Allah might not know something before it happens, even when you recite 'He knows all things'? What does this lesson reveal about that doubt, and will you commit to trusting His knowledge fully today?
?
When you sin, do you subconsciously think that Allah's knowledge is somehow incomplete or that He is learning about your actions as they occur? How does the truth of His eternal and unchanging knowledge change your understanding of accountability?
?
If you truly believed that Allah's knowledge is eternal and covers every detail of your past, present, and future, what would you stop worrying about? What would you start doing differently starting now?

Allah's Absolute Will and Its Scope
Affirmation of Allah's absolute will over all events with definitions of related terms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of Allah's will (al-irāda) as the third attribute of meanings, its distinction from power (al-qudra), and its absolute control over all events including good and evil, faith and disbelief.

Core Idea
Everything that occurs does so by Allah's will; nothing escapes His decree.

This passage from Ghazali's Qawaid al-Aqaid establishes the divine attribute of will and its comprehensive scope. It asserts that every event, from the smallest to the greatest, from good to evil, occurs only by Allah's decree and will. The footnotes clarify key concepts: the relationship between will and power, the meaning of decree and predetermination, and the nature of the cosmic will. You will see how the later scholars systematically defined these terms.

Guided Path
1
Read the main text and translation
Read the Arabic passage first, then the English translation. Notice how the main text makes a sweeping claim about Allah's will covering all categories of events.
The main text ends abruptly; the footnotes complete the thought.
2
Identify the key concepts in the footnotes
The footnotes (4) through (8) define will, distinguish it from power, explain decree and predetermination, and introduce the cosmic will. List each concept and its definition.
3
Understand the relationship between will and power
Note how footnote (4) explains that power brings things into existence or annihilates, while will specifies which possibility occurs. Power is subsidiary to will.
This is a key distinction in kalam.
4
Reflect on the phrase 'So what He wills is, and what He does not will is not'
This phrase summarizes the absolute nature of Allah's will. Consider its implications for human actions and the problem of evil.
The common misunderstanding is that humans act independently of Allah's will.
5
Analyze the definition of cosmic will
Footnote (8) defines the cosmic will as necessarily effective. When Allah wills something, its existence becomes necessary. Contrast this with human will.
This is a key theological point about divine determinism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإرادة (٤) :
وأنه تعالى مريد للكائنات (٥) مدبر للحادثات ، فلا يجرى في الملك والملكوت قليل أو كثير ، صغير أو كبير ، خير أو شر ، نفع أو ضر ، إيمان أو كفر ، عرفان أو نكر ، فوز أو خسران ، زيادة أو نقصان ، طاعة أو عصيان ، الا بقضائه وقدره (٦) ، وحكمته ومشيئته (۷) ، فما شاء كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن (۸) ، لا يخرج عن .
(٤) وهي الصفة الثالثة من صفات المعاني ، ويذكرها المتأخرون مع القدرة لتعلقهما بجميع الممكنات دون الواجبات والمستحيلات ، إلا أن جهة تعلقهما بالممكنات مختلفة ، فالقدرة صفة أزلية تؤثر في الممكن عند تعلقها به إيجاداً أو اعدما ؛ والارادة صفة أزلية تؤثر في اختصاص أحد طرفي الممكن من وجود وعدم أو طول وقصر ونحوها بالوقوع بدلا عن مقابله ، فصار تأثير القدرة فرع تأثير الارادة إذ لا يوجد عز وجل من الممكنات أو يعدم بقدرته ، إلا ما أراد تعالى وجوده أو اعدامه .
(٥) على الحقيقة والارادة شرط في كون كل فاعل فاعلا ، وكما لا يكون الفاعل إلا قادراً ، كذلك لا يكون إلا مريدا مختارا لفعله.
(٦) ومعنى قضائه تعالى : علمه أزلا بالاشياء على ما هي عليه ، ومعنى قدره ایجاده اياها على ما يطابق العلم.
(۷) ومشيئته هي والارادة مترادفتان ، أراد تعالى حدوث كل ما علم حدوثه على الوجه الذي علم حدوثه عليه ، ولا يكون في سلطانه الا ما يريد كونه ، ولا ينتفي من ملكه الا ما أراد انتفاءه.
(۸) وهذه هي الارادة الكونية ، ولا يتخلف متعلقها متى تعلقت بشيء وجب وجوده.
Will (4):
And that He, the Exalted, is the Willer of the existing things (5), the Manager of events. So nothing occurs in the dominion and sovereignty, little or much, small or great, good or evil, benefit or harm, faith or disbelief, recognition or denial, success or loss, increase or decrease, obedience or disobedience, except by His decree and predetermination (6), and His wisdom and will (7). So what He wills is, and what He does not will is not (8). Nothing escapes...
(4) It is the third attribute of the attributes of meanings. The later scholars mention it together with power, because both relate to all possible things, not to necessary or impossible things. However, the manner of their relation to possible things is different: power is an eternal attribute that affects the possible when it relates to it, by bringing into existence or annihilating; and will is an eternal attribute that affects the specification of one of the two sides of the possible (existence or non-existence, length or shortness, etc.) to occur instead of its opposite. So the effect of power is subsidiary to the effect of will, since He, the Mighty and Majestic, does not bring into existence or annihilate from among possible things by His power except what He wills to exist or annihilate.
(5) In reality, will is a condition for every agent to be an agent. Just as an agent cannot be except powerful, likewise he cannot be except willing and choosing his action.
(6) The meaning of His decree (qaḍāʾ) is His pre-eternal knowledge of things as they are, and the meaning of His predetermination (qadr) is His bringing them into existence in accordance with knowledge.
(7) His will (mashīʾa) and (irāda) are synonymous. He willed the occurrence of everything whose occurrence He knew, in the manner He knew it would occur. Nothing occurs in His dominion except what He wills to occur, and nothing is removed from His kingdom except what He wills to be removed.
(8) This is the cosmic will (al-irāda al-kawniyya), and its object never fails; when it is attached to something, its existence becomes necessary.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage affirms Allah's absolute will (al-irāda) over all events. It states that Allah is the Willer of all existing things and the Manager of events. Nothing occurs in the entire dominion (malakūt) and sovereignty (mulk) – regardless of category: little or much, good or evil, faith or disbelief, etc. – except by His decree (qaḍāʾ) and predetermination (qadr), His wisdom (ḥikma) and will (mashīʾa). The phrase 'فما شاء كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن' (So what He wills is, and what He does not will is not) summarizes absolute divine will. The footnotes provide detailed theological analysis: (4) defines will as the third attribute of meanings (after power and knowledge), noting that later scholars pair it with power because both relate to possible things, but their functions differ: power affects whether a thing exists or not, while will specifies which of the two possibilities occurs. Thus, power is subsidiary to will. (5) explains that will is a condition for any agent to be an agent, requiring both power and choice. (6) defines decree as Allah's pre-eternal knowledge of things, and predetermination as bringing them into existence matching that knowledge. (7) asserts that will (irāda) and wish (mashīʾa) are synonymous, and Allah wills everything that occurs in His dominion. (8) introduces the concept of cosmic will (al-irāda al-kawniyya), which is necessarily effective when attached to something. The passage thus emphasizes Allah's absolute control over all events, refuting any notion of independence from His will.

Key Terms
الإرادة
صفات المعاني
القدرة
القضاء
القدر
المشيئة
الإرادة الكونية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That human actions occur independently of Allah's will; that good and evil are not both from Allah.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that everything—including faith, disbelief, obedience, and disobedience—occurs only by Allah's decree and will. The cosmic will is absolutely effective.

Checkpoint
According to footnote (4), how does the effect of power relate to the effect of will?
A) Power is independent of will.
B) Power is subsidiary to will.
C) Will is subsidiary to power.
D) They are identical.

Key Takeaway
Allah's will is absolute and encompasses all events; power brings about existence or non-existence, but will specifies which one occurs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly believe that it occurred by Allah's will? How does that knowledge transform your repentance from mere regret to a plea for His mercy and a renewed determination to obey?
?
If Allah's will is always effective and nothing can resist it, why do you sometimes act as if your plans are more certain than His decree? What would change if you internalized that 'what Allah wills is, and what He does not will is not'?
?
The passage teaches that will is a necessary condition for any agent to act. Do you recognize that your own actions are meaningless without sincere intention? How can you align your will entirely with His, so that your desires become a reflection of His command?

Allah's Eternal and All-Encompassing Knowledge
Ghazali describes the scope and eternity of Allah's knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's knowledge is eternal and encompasses even the most hidden things, and that it is not acquired or subject to change.

Core Idea
Allah's knowledge is eternal, encompassing all that is hidden and manifest.

This passage from Imam al-Ghazali's Qawa'id al-'Aqa'id affirms the perfection of Allah's knowledge. It begins by giving vivid examples of things that are imperceptible to humans, then highlights that this knowledge is eternal and not acquired. The passage refutes any notion that Allah's knowledge is new or occurs through indwelling.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to grasp the vivid imagery and the theological claim.
Notice the rhythmic listing of examples.
2
Identify the examples of hidden knowledge
Identify the three examples: the black ant on a rock at night, the movement of motes in air, and the secret and what is more hidden. Reflect on why these were chosen.
They progressively emphasize the minuteness and secrecy of what Allah knows.
3
Understand the description of Allah's knowledge
Focus on the phrase 'علم قديم أزلي' and its negation of newness and indwelling (حلول) and transition (انتقال). Understand that this affirms the eternal and unchanging nature of divine knowledge.
The terms حلول and انتقال were used by some sects to claim that Allah acquires knowledge over time.
4
Reflect on the theological implication
Consider how this passage refutes any view that Allah's knowledge is limited or temporal, and reinforces tawhid and divine transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يعلم دبيب النملة السوداء على الصخرة الصماء في الليلة الظلماء (1) ويدرك حركة الذر في جو الهواء ويعلم السر وأخفى (2) ويطلع على هواجس الضمائر وحركات الخواطر وخفيات السرائر بعلم قديم أزلي لم يزل موصوفاً به في أزل الأزال لا يعلم متجدد حاصل في ذاته بالحلول والانتقال (3)
He knows the crawling of the black ant on the solid rock in the dark night (1), and perceives the movement of motes in the air, and knows the secret and what is more hidden (2), and is aware of the whispers of consciences and the movements of thoughts and the hidden depths of inner secrets, with an ancient eternal knowledge which He has never ceased to be described with in the eternity of eternities; He does not have a new knowledge occurring in His essence through indwelling and transition (3).
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage affirms that Allah's knowledge encompasses the most hidden things. It begins by giving examples: the crawling of a black ant on a rock in a dark night, the movement of dust motes in the air. Then it mentions that Allah knows the secret and what is even more hidden. He is aware of inner thoughts and hidden secrets. This knowledge is described as ancient and eternal (قديم أزلي); Allah has always been described with it in pre-eternity. It is not a new knowledge that occurs in His essence through indwelling (حلول) or transition (انتقال), refuting those who claim that Allah acquires knowledge over time (like Jahm ibn Safwan and the Rawafid). The passage emphasizes that Allah's knowledge is not acquired or developed; it is eternal and all-encompassing.

أزل الأزال
حلول
انتقال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah's knowledge is acquired or occurs anew in time.
Correction: The passage states that Allah's knowledge is 'قديم أزلي' (ancient eternal) and not 'متجدد' (new), and it does not occur through indwelling (حلول) or transition (انتقال).

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the nature of Allah's knowledge?
A) It is new and occurs in His essence.
B) It is eternal and not subject to change.
C) It is limited to major events.
D) It is acquired through learning.

Key Takeaway
Allah's knowledge is eternal and encompasses all hidden and manifest things; it is not acquired or subject to change.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage says Allah knows 'what is more hidden'—the whispers of your heart that even you may not admit. Are there hidden intentions or desires you are harboring that oppose His commands? What will you do to purify them?
?
Allah's knowledge is not new; it does not change with time. He knew every moment of your life before you lived it. Does this realization fill you with awe and motivate you to live a life pleasing to Him? What concrete step will you take this week to act upon this reality?

Everything Occurs by Allah's Will
Ghazali enumerates the comprehensiveness of Allah's will through a list of opposites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's will encompasses all events and that nothing falls outside His decree and plan.

Core Idea
Allah's will is absolute—nothing happens without His permission and decree.

Imam Ghazali opens this section by affirming the attribute of will for Allah. He begins with a sweeping statement that Allah is the Willer of all contingent beings and the Director of all originated events. To leave no room for doubt, he enumerates a comprehensive list of opposites, showing that from the smallest to the greatest, every occurrence—whether good or evil, faith or disbelief, obedience or sin—takes place only by Allah's decree and will. This lesson examines that foundational principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and notice the opening declaration
Read the Arabic and translation, noting how Ghazali begins with Allah as willing and directing all things.
2
Identify the extensive list of opposites
Find the list of pairs (e.g., good/evil, faith/disbelief) and reflect on why Ghazali includes them. They cover every possible category.
The list is comprehensive to show that no domain is excluded.
3
Understand the key phrase 'fama sha'a kana'
This is the core principle: whatever Allah wills is, and whatever He does not will is not. Memrise this phrase.
It summarizes the absolute sovereignty of His will.
4
Recognize the exclusion of even subtle events
Ghazali says that not even a glance or stray thought escapes His will. This emphasizes the all-encompassing nature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإرادة (4): وأنه تعالى مريد للكائنات (5) مدبر للحادثات فلا يجرى في الملك والملكوت قليل أو كثير صغير أو كبير خير أو شر نفع أو ضر إيمان أو كفر عرفان أو نكر فوز أو خسران زيادة أو نقصان طاعة أو عصيان إلا بقضائه وقدره (6) وحكمته ومشيئته (7) فما شاء كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن (8) لا يخرج عن مشيئته لفتة ناظر ولا فلتة خاطر بل هو المبدىء المعيد الفعال لما يريد (1) لا راد لأمره ولا معقب لقضائه ولا مهرب لعبد عن معصيته إلا بتوفيقه ورحمته ولا قوة له على طاعته إلا بمشيئته (2) وارادته فلو اجتمع الانس والجن والملائكة والشياطين على أن يحركوا في العالم ذرة أو يسكنوها دون ارادته ومشيئته لعجزوا عن ذلك (3) وأن ارادته قائمة بذاته في جملة صفاته (4) لم يزل كذلك موصوفاً بها (5) مريدا في أزله لوجود الاشياء في أوقاتها التي قدرها فوجدت في أوقاتها كما أراده في أزله من غير تقدم ولا تأخر بل وقعت على وفق علمه وإرادته (6) من غير تبدل ولا تغير دبر الأمور لا بترتيب أفكار ولا تربص (7) زمان فلذلك لم يشغله شأن شأن عن
(The Will) (4): And that He, exalted, is willing for all contingent beings (5), directing all originated events. So nothing occurs in the kingdom and dominion, little or much, small or great, good or evil, benefit or harm, faith or disbelief, recognition or denial, success or loss, increase or decrease, obedience or disobedience, except by His decree and predestination (6), His wisdom and will (7). So whatever He wills is, and whatever He does not will is not (8). Nothing falls outside: His will does not miss the glance of a looker, nor a stray thought (1). Rather, He is the Originator, the Reproducer, the Doer of what He wills (1). There is no repeller of His command, no averter of His decree. There is no escape for a servant from his sin except by His success and mercy, and no strength for him to obey Him except by His will (2) and desire. If all of mankind, jinn, angels, and devils were to gather to move a single atom in the world or to keep it still without His will and desire, they would be incapable of that (3). And that His will subsists in His essence among His attributes (4). He has never ceased to be described thus (5), willing in pre-eternity the existence of things at their decreed times, so they exist at their times as He willed in pre-eternity without advance or delay. Rather, they occur in accordance with His knowledge and will (6), without change or alteration. He manages affairs without arrangement of thoughts or waiting of time (7). Therefore, no occupation diverts Him from another.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage affirms the attribute of will (irada) for Allah. It begins by stating that Allah is mureed (willing) for all contingent beings and is the director of all originated events. Then it lists a wide range of opposites to emphasize that nothing—whether good or evil, faith or disbelief, etc.—occurs except by His decree (qada) and predestination (qadr), His wisdom and will. The phrase 'fama sha'a kana wa ma lam yasha' lam yakun' encapsulates the absolute sovereignty of His will. The passage then emphasizes that not even the slightest thought escapes His will. He is the originator and reiterator, the doer of whatever He wills. No one can repel His command or reverse His decree. The servant's avoidance of sin is only through Allah's tawfiq (success) and mercy, and his strength to obey is only through His will. Then comes a powerful illustration: if all created beings—humans, jinn, angels, devils—tried to move or still a single atom without His will, they would be utterly incapable. This demonstrates that all action is dependent on His will. The will is then described as an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence. He has always been described with it. He willed in pre-eternity the existence of things at their precisely determined times, and they come into existence exactly as willed, without any change or delay. His management of affairs is not through sequential planning or waiting, which implies timelessness and limitless power.

Correction: The passage explicitly includes 'evil' and 'disobedience' in the list of things that occur only by His will. This does not mean He approves of evil, but that His will is all-encompassing.

The Absolute Sovereignty of Allah's Will
Ghazali emphasizes the absolute sovereignty of Allah's will over all creatures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that no being can oppose Allah's will and that all creatures are utterly dependent on His will for any action.

Core Idea
All creation combined cannot move an atom without Allah's will.

Having established that every event occurs by Allah's will, Imam Ghazali now emphasizes the absolute sovereignty of that will. He declares that there is no repeller of Allah's command and no averter of His decree. He then highlights the human condition: a servant can only avoid sin through Allah's tawfiq (grace) and can only obey through His will. To drive the point home, he presents a striking illustration: if all of humanity, jinn, angels, and devils gathered to move or still a single atom against Allah's will, they would be utterly incapable. This lesson examines those powerful statements.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the introductory affirmations
Notice the titles: Originator, Reproducer, Doer of what He wills. These emphasize His absolute creative power.
2
Understand the statements about no repeller and no averter
No one can repel His command or reverse His decree. This highlights His absolute authority.
3
Reflect on human dependence on Allah's tawfiq
The passage says that a servant cannot escape sin except by Allah's tawfiq and mercy, and cannot obey except by His will. This shows total dependence.
4
Analyze the atom illustration
If all creatures gathered to move or still a single atom without Allah's will, they would fail. This demonstrates the limitlessness of divine power.
The atom is chosen as the smallest particle to underline the point.

(The Will) (4): And that He, exalted, is willing for all contingent beings (5), directing all originated events. So nothing occurs in the kingdom and dominion, little or much, small or great, good or evil, benefit or harm, faith or disbelief, recognition or denial, success or loss, increase or decrease, obedience or disobedience, except by His decree and predestination (6), His wisdom and will (7). So whatever He wills is, and whatever He does not will is not (8). Nothing falls outside: His will does not miss the glance of a looker, nor a stray thought (1). There is no escape for a servant from his sin except by His success and mercy, and no strength for him to obey Him except by His will (2) and desire. Rather, they occur in accordance with His knowledge and will (6), without change or alteration. He manages affairs without arrangement of thoughts or waiting of time (7). The Eternal and Timeless Nature of Allah's Will
Ghazali explains that Allah's will is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, with pre-eternal willing and timeless management.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's will is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, and that His willing in pre-eternity determines the timing of all events without any change.

Core Idea
Allah's will is eternal and timeless; He willed everything in pre-eternity exactly as it occurs.

The final part of this section moves from the scope and sovereignty of Allah's will to its nature. Imam Ghazali explains that the will is an attribute that subsists in Allah's essence from eternity. He has always been described as 'willing.' In pre-eternity, He willed the existence of things at their specific times, and accordingly, they come into existence precisely when He ordained, without advance or delay. Moreover, His management of affairs is not through sequential thought or waiting, which underscores His timelessness and limitless power. This lesson delves into the eternal and timeless quality of the divine will.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the claim that will subsists in Allah's essence
The passage says 'His will subsists in His essence among His attributes.' This is a key theological point: the attributes are not separate from Allah.
2
Understand that Allah has never ceased to be described as willing
He has always been 'mureed' (willing). This means the attribute is eternal, not acquired in time.
3
Grasp the concept of pre-eternal willing
He willed in pre-eternity the existence of things at their decreed times, so they occur exactly as willed without advance or delay.
This connects the eternal will with temporal events.
4
Notice the timeless management without thought or waiting
He manages affairs without arranging thoughts or waiting for time. This shows His power is immediate and limitless.
The closing line implies He can attend to all matters simultaneously.

Divine Attributes

6 min
The Divine Attribute of Will (Irada)
Imam Ghazali defines the divine will and its scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's will is an eternal, all-encompassing attribute that governs all existence, including human actions, and that nothing occurs outside His will.

Core Idea
Allah's will is eternal and decisive; nothing happens without it.

Imam Ghazali begins by affirming that Allah's will is not like human will—it is not momentary or incidental. He then expands on its scope, emphasizing that every event, including sins, occurs only by His will. This passage lays the foundation for understanding divine decree (qadar) and the relationship between God's will and human actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Ghazali uses a very precise and refutational style.
2
Identify the key characteristics of Allah's will
Look for descriptions: not a glance, no repeller, eternal, subsisting in His essence, in accordance with knowledge.
3
Understand the refutation of false views
Note that the passage rejects the idea that sins occur without Allah's will, and that God can will something that does not happen.
This is a direct refutation of the Qadariyya and Mu'tazila.
4
Reflect on the implications for human responsibility
Consider how divine will and human power relate, as mentioned with 'no escape from sin except by His success.'
This touches on the delicate balance between divine will and human responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مشيئته لفتة ناظر ، ولا فلتة خاطر بل هو المبدىء المعيد ، الفعال لما يريد (١) ، لا راد لأمره ، ولا معقب لقضائه ، ولا مهرب لعبد عن معصيته إلا بتوفيقه ورحمته ، ، ولا قوة له على طاعته الا بمشيئته (۲) وارادته ، فلو اجتمع الانس والجن والملائكة والشياطين على أن يحركوا في العالم ذرة أو يسكنوها دون ارادته ومشيئته لعجزوا عن ذلك (۳) وأن ارادته قائمة بذاته في جملة صفاته (٤) ، لم يزل كذلك موصوفاً بها (٥) ، مريدا في أزله لوجود الاشياء في أوقاتها التي قدرها فوجدت في أوقاتها كما أراده في أزله من غير تقدم ولا تأخر ، بل وقعت على وفق علمه وإرادته (٦) ، من غير تبدل ولا تغير ، دبر الأمور لا بترتيب أفكار ، ولا تربص (۷) زمان ، فلذلك لم يشغله شأن شأن عن (١) خلافا لمن زعم أن المعاصي كلها كانت من غير مشيئة له فيها ، وقد يريد كون الشيء فلا يكون . (۲) وفي نسخة اخرى : ولا قوة له على طاعته الا بمحبته وإرادته وهذا المعنى هو تفسير : لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله . (۳) فلا يجري في ملكه شيء إلا بمشيئته في أقضيته ومراداته سبحانه جل شأنه (٤) كالعلم ، والقدرة ، والسمع والبصر والكلام . • (٥) موصوفا بها في الازل كما أنه لم يزل عالما بعلم ، محيط بجميع المعلومات على التفصيل ، وكما أنه لم يزل ، رائيا برؤية محيط بجميع ، سامعا بسمع قادرا بقدرة شاملة لجميع المقدورات على التفصيل ، سامعا المسموعات والمرئيات على التفصيل (٦) وتأثير الإرادة عند أهل الحق على وفق العلم ، فكل ما علم الله تعالى أنه يكون من الممكنات أو لا يكون فذلك مراده عز وجل (۷) وفي نسخة أخرى : لا بترتيب أفكار ، وتربص زمان والمراد : لما كان التدبير في صفات البشر هو التفكر في عواقب الامور ، ولا يوصف سبحانه وتعالى به فإنه لم يزل عالما قبل وقوعها ، فلذلك أعقبه بقوله « لا بترتيب أفكار وتربص زمان » لهذا كان المراد بالتدبير في الأمور هنا امضاؤها ، وبه فسر قوله تعالى : يدبر الامر من السماء الى الأرض فيكون المدبر على هذا من أوصافه المشتقة من فعله ولا يكون من أوصافه الازلية ؛ أو بمعنى دبر الامور علم بها ، فعلى هذا يكون المدير من أسمائه الازلية ، فلا مدبر ولا مقدر لما يجري من السموات والارض غيره ، كل حادث فيهن وما بينهن واقع بتقديره، وجار على تدبيره ، فله التدبير والتقدير
His will is not a glance of an eye nor a passing thought, but He is the Originator, the Restorer, the Doer of whatever He wills (1). There is no repeller of His command, no annuller of His decree, and no escape for a servant from his sin except through His success and mercy. And no power for a servant upon his obedience except by His will (2) and His desire. So if humans, jinn, angels, and devils gathered to move a single atom in the universe or to make it still without His desire and will, they would be incapable of that (3). And His desire is subsisting in His essence among His attributes (4). He has not ceased to be described by them (5), willing in His pre-eternity the existence of things at their times which He decreed, so they came into existence at their times as He willed in His pre-eternity without advance or delay; rather they occurred according to His knowledge and will (6), without change or alteration. He manages affairs without the arrangement of thoughts nor the waiting of time (7). Therefore, no matter occupies Him from another matter. (1) Contrary to those who claim that all sins occur without His will, and [they claim] He may will a thing to be and it is not. (2) In another version: 'And no power for a servant upon his obedience except by His love and His will,' and this meaning is the interpretation of 'There is no power and no strength except with Allah.' (3) So nothing runs in His kingdom except by His will in His decrees and desires, exalted is He, great is His majesty. (4) Such as knowledge, power, hearing, sight, and speech. (5) Described by them in pre-eternity, just as He has not ceased to be knowing with knowledge encompassing all known things in detail, and as He has not ceased to be seeing with sight encompassing all visible things, hearing with hearing, powerful with power comprehensive of all possible things in detail, hearing audible things and seeing visible things in detail. (6) The effect of will according to the people of truth is in accordance with knowledge; so whatever Allah Almighty knows will be from possibles or not be, that is His will, Mighty and Majestic. (7) In another version: 'without the arrangement of thoughts and the waiting of time.' And the intended meaning: since management in human attributes is reflecting upon consequences of matters, and He, glorified and exalted, is not described with that, for He has not ceased to be knowing before their occurrence, therefore He followed it with His saying 'without arrangement of thoughts and waiting of time.' Hence, management of affairs here means their execution, and with this the verse 'He manages the affair from the heaven to the earth' is interpreted. So 'the Manager' according to this is among His attributes derived from His action and not from His pre-eternal attributes; or it means He knew the affairs, and according to this, 'the Director' is among His pre-eternal names. So there is no manager nor arranger for what occurs from the heavens and the earth other than Him; every event in them and between them occurs by His decree and runs by His management. So to Him belongs management and decree.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage defines the divine attribute of will (irāda) and its implications. It begins by affirming that God's will is not momentary or incidental but eternal and decisive. The author refutes the view that sins occur without God's will, emphasizing that nothing happens except by His will. He then explains that God's will is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, like other attributes. The passage also clarifies that God's will is in accordance with His knowledge, and that His management of affairs is not like human reflection. The footnotes expand on these points, including variant readings and further refutations. The overall argument is that God's will is all-encompassing, eternal, and perfectly aligned with His knowledge.

Key Terms
مشيئة
إرادة
صفات المعاني
أزل
تقدير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God does not will sinful acts; they occur outside His will.
Correction: The passage explicitly refutes this, stating that no escape from sin is possible except by God's will, and that all sins occur by His will, as He is the Doer of whatever He wills.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relationship between God's will and the occurrence of sins?
A) Sins occur without His will.
B) Sins occur only by His will.
C) God wills only good deeds.
D) Sins are outside His knowledge.

Key Takeaway
Allah's will is eternal, all-encompassing, and in perfect accordance with His knowledge; nothing in creation occurs outside of it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your every act of obedience is only possible by Allah's will, do you truly depend on Him for each prayer, each good deed, or do you rely on your own strength? Before your next action, consciously attribute to Him the ability to do it.
?
Since even your sins occur within Allah's will, do you use that as an excuse to sin, or does it drive you to seek His mercy with greater desperation? What sin have you treated as if Allah had no part in it, and what does that reveal about your belief in His absolute sovereignty?
?
The passage says there is 'no escape for a servant from his sin except through His success and mercy.' How does that make you feel about the sins you have committed? Will you today beg Allah for His 'tawfiq' (success) to abandon a specific sin, knowing you cannot do it without His will?

The Divine Attributes of Hearing and Sight
Imam Ghazali defines the attributes of hearing and sight.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's attributes of hearing and sight are eternal, perfect, and entirely unlike human senses, and why this is essential for tawhid.

Core Idea
Allah hears and sees all, but not as we do.

Imam Ghazali now turns to the divine attributes of hearing and sight. He begins by affirming that God perceives all things without limitation, then clarifies that this perception is not through physical organs. This passage establishes the transcendence of Allah's attributes and guards against anthropomorphism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without over-analyzing. Then read the English translation. Let the full picture of God's hearing and sight come through.
2
Identify the affirmations and negations
Notice what the passage affirms (Allah hears and sees everything) and what it negates (no physical organs, no limitations like distance or darkness).
This is the core of tanzih (transcendence).
3
Understand the definition as eternal attributes
The passage defines hearing and sight as eternal attributes subsisting in God's essence. Reflect on what this means: they are not acquired or dependent on anything.
These are attributes of ma‘ani (meanings) according to the Ash‘ari framework.
4
Reflect on the contrast with creatures
The passage ends by contrasting divine attributes with human senses. Ask yourself: why is this contrast necessary? It protects God's uniqueness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السمع والبصر (١) : وأنه تعالى سميع بصير يسمع ويرى ، لا يعزب عن سمعه مسموع وان خفى ، ولا يغيب عن رؤيته مرئى وإن دقّ (۲) ، ولا يحجب سمعه بعد ، ولا يدفع رؤيته ظلام يرى من غير حدقة وأجفان ، ويسمع من غير أصمخة (۳) وآذان ، كما يعلم بغير قلب ، ويبطش بغير جارحة ، ويخلق بغير آلة ، إذ لا تشبه صفاته صفات الخلق ، كما لا تشبه ذاته ذوات الخلق(٤) . (۱) وهما الصفة الرابعة والخامسة من صفات المعاني المتعلقان بجميع الموجودات وحقيقة السمع صفة أزلية قائمة بذاته تعالى تتعلق بالموجودات ، فتدرك الموجودات ادراكاً تاما ، لا على سبيل التخيل والتوهم ولا على طريق تأثير حاسة ولا وصول هواء وحقيقة البصر : صفة أزلية قائمة بذاته تعالى تتعلق بالموجودات فتدرك الموجودات ادراكاً تاما لا على سبيل التخيل والتوهم ، ولا على سبيل طريق تأثر حاسة ولا وصول شعاع، ومعنى المتعلقات الطالبان بالانكشاف الجميع الموجودات (۲) كالذرة في الهواء يسمع النداء ويجيب الدعاء . Hearing and Sight (1): And that He, exalted, is Hearing, Seeing; He hears and sees. No audible thing escapes His hearing, even if hidden, and no visible thing is absent from His sight, even if small (2). Distance does not veil His hearing, nor does darkness repel His sight. He sees without pupil and eyelids, and hears without ear canals (3) and ears, just as He knows without a heart, and strikes without a limb, and creates without a tool. For His attributes do not resemble the attributes of creation, just as His essence does not resemble the essences of creation (4). (1) They are the fourth and fifth attributes of the attributes of meanings, related to all existents. The reality of hearing is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, related to existents, so it perceives existents with complete perception, not by way of imagination or illusion, nor by the effect of a sense or the arrival of air. And the reality of sight: an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, related to existents, so it perceives existents with complete perception, not by way of imagination or illusion, nor by the effect of a sense or the arrival of a ray. And the meaning of the two relations is the disclosure of all existents. (2) Like the atom in the air, He hears the call and answers the supplication. (3) Plural of ṣimākh, meaning the hole in the ear. (4) For His knowledge is not like the knowledge of creatures, which differs in its location, whether it is the brain or the heart, nor like the hearing of a creature, which is a power lodged in the concavity of the ear canal, whose perception of sounds depends on the air conveying them to the sense and the effect of the sense, nor like the sight of a creature, which is a power lodged in the two hollow nerves extending from the brain. Therefore, His attributes do not resemble the attributes of creation, just as His essence does not resemble the essence of creation, because His transcendence and sanctity from what is not befitting Him is established, exalted is His majesty.

Commentary
This passage defines the divine attributes of hearing (samʿ) and sight (baṣar). It begins by affirming that God hears all sounds and sees all things, no matter how small, without being hindered by distance or darkness. It then clarifies that God's hearing and sight are not through physical organs like ears and eyes, just as His knowledge is without a heart and His action without tools. The footnotes expand on the definition: hearing and sight are eternal attributes subsisting in God's essence, perceiving all existents perfectly without physical processes. The passage concludes by emphasizing that divine attributes do not resemble those of creatures, as God is transcendent above all anthropomorphic qualities.

The Eternal Speech of Allah
Ghazali defines divine speech as eternal and lists its negations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's attribute of speech is eternal, subsisting in His essence, and unlike created speech in being free from letters, sounds, and change.

Core Idea
Allah's speech is eternal, not created, and incomparable to human speech.

In this passage, Imam Ghazali defines the divine attribute of speech (kalām). He establishes that Allah is described as 'speaker' with an eternal speech that subsists in His essence. This speech relates to all things known and is free from any imperfection or change. The passage also provides a rational proof: the term 'speaker' necessarily implies the attribute of speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own definition and negations sink in.
Notice the list of negations towards the end.
2
Identify the definition of divine speech
Find where Ghazali defines speech and note the key phrases: 'eternal, pre-existent speech subsisting in His essence' and that it is the sixth attribute of the attributes of meanings.
3
List what divine speech does not admit
Go through the list: non-existence, silence, renewal, partiality, totality, precedence, delay, solecism, grammatical inflection, letters, sounds, and other changes. Note how this distinguishes it from created speech.
4
Understand the rational proof
The passage ends with a proof: the term 'speaker' (mutakallim) is derived from speech (kalām). Affirming the derived term for Allah indicates the existence of the source attribute, just as 'knower' implies knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام (ه) : وأنه تعالى متكلم آمر ناه ، واعد متوعد ، بكلام أزلي قديم قائم بذاته (٦) (٥) وهي الصفة السادسة من صفات المعاني ، وهي صفة أزلية قائمة بذاته تتعلق بما تعلق به العلم ، وهو كل واجب ، وكل مستحيل ، وكل جائز ، لا تقبل العدم ، ولا ما في معناه من السكوت ولا التجديد ولا البعض ، ولا الكل ولا التقديم ولا التأخير ، ولا اللحن ولا الاعراب ولا الحرف ولا الصوت ولا سائر أنواع التغييرات (٦) لأن ثبوت المشتق للشيء يدل على ثبوت مأخذ الاشتقاق لذلك الشيء
Speech (5): And that He, exalted, is a speaker, a commander, a prohibitor, a promiser, a threatener, with an eternal, pre-existent speech subsisting in His essence (6). (5) It is the sixth attribute of the attributes of meanings, and it is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, related to what knowledge relates to—which is every necessary, every impossible, and every possible. It does not admit non-existence, nor what is in its meaning of silence, nor renewal, nor partiality, nor totality, nor precedence, nor delay, nor solecism, nor grammatical inflection, nor letters, nor sounds, nor all other types of changes. (6) Because the affirmation of a derived term for something indicates the affirmation of the source of derivation for that thing.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage defines the divine attribute of speech (kalām). It begins by stating that God is a speaker who commands, prohibits, promises, and threatens with an eternal speech subsisting in His essence. The footnote (5) explains that speech is the sixth attribute of the attributes of meanings, eternal and subsisting in God's essence. It relates to everything that knowledge relates to: the necessary, the impossible, and the possible. This speech does not admit of non-existence, silence, renewal, or any change such as letters, sounds, or grammatical inflection. Footnote (6) provides a rational proof: if God is described as 'speaker' (mutakallim), that requires the existence of speech (kalām) as an attribute, just as 'knower' requires knowledge. This passage emphasizes God's speech is unlike created speech, being eternal and not composed of letters or sounds.

Key Takeaway
Allah's speech is an eternal attribute not composed of letters or sounds.

The Eternal Speech of God and the Quran
Ghazali defines God's eternal speech and its relation to scriptures

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic doctrine that God's speech is an eternal, uncreated attribute subsisting in His essence, and how the Quran we recite is a created expression of that eternal speech.

Core Idea
God's speech is eternal; the Quran we recite is its created expression.

This passage from Imam al-Ghazali's Qawa'id al-Aqa'id lays out the foundational Sunni belief about the divine attribute of speech. It affirms that God speaks with an eternal speech that is not like created sounds or letters. The passage then clarifies the relationship between this eternal speech and the revealed books, especially the Quran, addressing a common confusion about whether the recited Quran is created or uncreated.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the connective 'wa anna' which introduces each point.
2
Identify the core affirmation
Find where Ghazali states that God is speaking with an eternal speech subsisting in His essence. This is the foundation.
3
Understand the negation of resemblance
Notice how he distinguishes God's speech from created speech: no sound, no air, no letters.
4
Grasp the expression distinction
The passage clarifies that the Quran, Torah, etc., are expressions of the eternal speech; the expressions are created, but the meaning in God is uncreated.
This resolves the common misunderstanding.
5
Reflect on Moses hearing
Consider how Moses heard God's speech without sound or letter, analogous to seeing God in the afterlife without physical attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام (ه) : وأنه تعالى متكلم آمر ناه واعد متوعد بكلام أزلي قديم قائم بذاته (٦) . (٦) لأن ثبوت المشتق للشيء يدل على ثبوت مأخذ الاشتقاق لذلك الشيء . لا يشبه كلام الخلق، فليس بصوت يحدث من انسلال هواء أو اصطكاك أجرام، ولا بحرف ينقطع باطباق شفة أو تحريك لسان (۱)، وأن القرآن والتوراة والانجيل والزبور كتبه المنزلة على رسله عليهم السلام (۲)، وأن القرآن مقروء بالألسنة مكتوب في المصاحف، محفوظ في القلوب (۳)، وأنه مع ذلك قديم قائم بذات الله تعالى، لا يقبل الانفصال والافتراق، بالانتقال إلى القلوب والأوراق (٤)، وأن موسى سمع كلام الله بغير صوت ولا حرف، كما يرى الأبرار ذات الله تعالى في الآخرة (٥) من غير جوهر ولا عرض . (۱) إذ كلام الخلق كله عرض، وكلام الله تعالى لا يوصف بجسم ولا عرض، ولهذا بين الامام الغزالي رضي الله عنه وجه عدم شبهه كلام الخلق فقال : ه فليس بصوت يحدث من بين انسلال هواء، أو اصطكال أجرام، ولا بحرف يتقطع باطباق شفة أو تحرك لسان، فكل ذلك من صفات كلام الخلق . (۲) لأن الحروف إنما هي عبارة عنه، والعبارة غير المعبر عنه، فلذلك اختلفت باختلاف الالسنة، وإذا عبرت عن تلك الصفة القائمة بذاته تعالى بالعربية فقرآن، وبالعبرانية فتوراة، وبالسريانية فانجيل وزبور، والاختلاف في العبارات دون المسمى، فحروف القرآن حادثة والمعبر عنه بها هو المعنى القائم بذات الله تعالى قديم، فالتلاوة والقراءة والكتابة حادثة ، والمتلو والمقروء والمكتوب قديم . وبيان المراد : أن ما دلت عليه الكتابة والقراءة والتلاوة ، كما إذا ذكر الله بألسنة متعددة ولغات مختلفة فإن الذكر حادث والمذكور وهو رب العالمين قديم . (۳) وفي نسخة أخرى : محفوظ في القلوب والصدور . (٤) كما لا يقبل العدم ولا ما في معناه من السكوت ، ولا التجديد ، ولا البعض ولا الكل ، ولا التقديم ولا التأخير، ولا اللحن ولا الاعراب ، ولا سائر التغييرات . (٥) رؤية تليق بذاته تعالى .
Speech (5): And that He, exalted, is Speaking, commanding, forbidding, promising, threatening, with an eternal, pre-eternal speech subsisting in His essence (6). (6) Because the affirmation of the derived term for something indicates the affirmation of the source of derivation for that thing. It does not resemble the speech of creation, for it is not a sound arising from the escape of air or the striking of bodies, nor a letter cut off by the closure of a lip or the movement of a tongue (1). And that the Qur'an, the Torah, the Gospel, and the Psalms are His books revealed to His messengers, peace be upon them (2). And that the Qur'an is read by tongues, written in manuscripts, preserved in hearts (3). And that despite that, it is pre-eternal, subsisting in God's essence, not accepting separation or division by transfer to hearts and pages (4). And that Moses heard God's speech without sound or letter, just as the righteous will see God's essence in the afterlife (5) without substance or accident. (1) For all speech of creation is an accident, and God's speech is not described as a body or accident. Therefore, Imam al-Ghazali, may God be pleased with him, explained the aspect of its dissimilarity to created speech, saying: it is not a sound arising from the escape of air or the striking of bodies, nor a letter cut off by the closure of a lip or the movement of a tongue; all of that is from the attributes of created speech. (2) Because letters are only expressions of it, and the expression is other than the expressed. Therefore, they differ with the difference of languages: when expressed in Arabic, it is the Qur'an; in Hebrew, the Torah; in Syriac, the Gospel and Psalms. The difference is in the expressions, not in the named referent. So the letters of the Qur'an are originated, but the expressed referent—the meaning subsisting in God's essence—is pre-eternal. Thus recitation, reading, and writing are originated, while the recited, read, and written is pre-eternal. The explanation of the intended meaning: that what writing, reading, and recitation indicate—just as when God is mentioned in multiple tongues and different languages—the mention is originated, while the mentioned—the Lord of the worlds—is pre-eternal. (3) In another copy: preserved in hearts and chests. (4) Just as it does not accept non-existence nor what is in its meaning of silence, nor renewal, nor partiality, nor totality, nor precedence, nor delay, nor solecism, nor inflection, nor other changes. (5) A vision befitting His essence.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage defines the divine attribute of speech (al-kalām) and clarifies its nature. It begins by affirming that God is speaking (mutakallim) with an eternal, pre-eternal speech subsisting in His essence. The reason given (footnote 6) is that if we call God 'Speaking,' the derived term implies the existence of the source (kalām) in Him. Then it negates likeness to created speech: it is not a sound produced by air or striking bodies, nor a letter formed by lips or tongue (footnote 1 expands that created speech is an accident, while God's speech is neither body nor accident). The passage then addresses the revealed books: the Qur'an, Torah, Gospel, and Psalms are His books. Yet the Qur'an is read, written, and memorized, but still pre-eternal in God's essence, not subject to separation or change (footnote 4 lists what it does not accept: non-existence, silence, renewal, etc.). The key distinction (footnote 2) is that letters are expressions of the eternal speech; the expression is created, the expressed meaning is pre-eternal. Thus the recited Qur'an is created, but what it signifies—the eternal attribute—is uncreated. Finally, Moses heard God's speech without sound or letter, analogous to how the righteous will see God without physical attributes. The passage carefully distinguishes between the eternal speech as an attribute and its temporal expressions.

Key Terms
الكلام
القول القديم
عبارة
معنى قائم بالذات
القرآن
التوراة
سامع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran we recite is itself the eternal, uncreated speech of God.
Correction: The Quran as recited, written, and memorized is a created expression of the eternal speech. The letters and sounds are temporal, while the meaning subsisting in God's essence is uncreated.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the relationship between the written Qur'an and God's eternal speech?
A) The written Qur'an is exactly the same as God's eternal speech, uncreated.
B) The written Qur'an is a created expression that symbolizes the uncreated, eternal speech.
C) The written Qur'an is a separate entity that has no connection to God's speech.
D) The written Qur'an is an accident that God creates directly without any eternal attribute.

Key Takeaway
God's speech is an eternal, uncreated attribute; the Quran we recite is its created expression, not the attribute itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Qur'an, do you ever pause to consider that the very words your tongue utters are created expressions of an eternal reality that subsists in God Himself? How does that awareness transform your recitation from a mere act into a connection with the divine essence?
?
If God's speech is utterly beyond sound and letters, what does that imply about the nature of divine revelation and its authority? Are you tempted to reduce God's word to a human book, or do you truly revere it as the uncreated meaning behind the created text?
?
Moses heard God's speech without any auditory or physical medium. How does that challenge your assumptions about how God communicates with His creation? Are you willing to accept that the deepest truths from God may surpass your sensory and intellectual frameworks?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
5 min
God's Attributes Are Real and Additional to His Essence
Ghazali concludes that God is Living, Knowing, etc., by distinct attributes, not by mere essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that in Ash'ari theology, God's attributes are real, eternal, and distinct from His essence, not merely conceptual or identical to it.

Core Idea
God's attributes are real perfections added to His essence, not the essence itself.

In this concluding passage of the section on divine attributes, Ghazali consolidates the Ash'ari position. He affirms that God is described by each attribute (life, power, knowledge, etc.) in a real sense, not merely as a logical consequence of His essence. The accompanying scholar's note explains that these 'attributes of meanings' are additional to the essence, eternally subsisting in it as perfections.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once through. Then read the English translation. Notice the key phrase 'not by mere essence' (lā bi-mujarrad al-dhāt).
The passage is short but dense. Take your time.
2
Identify the main claim
The passage states that God is Living, Knowing, etc., by distinct attributes, not by His essence alone. This is a direct rejection of the view that attributes are identical to the essence.
Compare with the footnote which expands on this.
3
Understand the footnote's clarification
The footnote explicitly says the 'attributes of meanings' are additional (zāʼida) to the essence. Each attribute is a real, eternal perfection; their opposites would be defects.
This affirms the Ash'ari position that attributes are distinct yet not separate.
4
Reflect on the theological significance
This passage guards against two extremes: reducing attributes to mere names (Mu'tazilite) or imagining them as independent entities (anthropomorphism).
Ash'aris hold a middle ground: real, eternal, but subsisting in the essence.
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to ensure you grasp the core idea. Then try the activity.
The activity will deepen your engagement with the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا كانت له هذه الصفات كان حيا ، عالما ، قادراً ، مريداً ، سميعاً ، بصيراً ، متكلما ، بالحياة والقدرة ، والعلم ، والإرادة والسمع والبصر ، والكلام ، لا بمجرد الذات (٦) . (٦) أشار المؤلف بذلك الى أن صفات المعاني زائدة على الذات العلية، بأن المعنى الذي يفهم من العلم أبلغ من القدرة الذي هو التمكن من الفعل أو الترك، وكذا باقي صفات المعاني فانها صفات ثابتة موجودة في نفسها قديمة باقية بالذات العلية وهي كمالات ونقائضها نقائض، والله تعالى منزه عن النقائض .
And since He possesses these attributes, He is Living, Knowing, Willing, Hearing, Seeing, Speaking—by life, power, knowledge, will, hearing, sight, and speech, not by mere essence (6). (6) The author indicated by this that the attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-ma‘ānī) are additional to the exalted essence. For the meaning understood from knowledge is more comprehensive than power, which is the ability to act or abstain; and likewise the rest of the attributes of meanings, for they are attributes established, existing in themselves, pre-eternal, abiding with the exalted essence. They are perfections, and their opposites are defects. God is transcendent above defects.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This concluding passage ties together the attributes discussed earlier. It states that because God has these attributes (life, power, knowledge, will, hearing, sight, speech), He is described as Living, Knowing, Powerful, etc. These descriptions are not by mere essence but by distinct, eternal attributes that subsist in His essence. The commentary (footnote 6) explicitly affirms that the 'attributes of meanings' (ṣifāt al-ma‘ānī)—the same attributes listed—are additional to the essence (zāʼida ʻalā al-dhāt). Each attribute is a real, eternal perfection, and their opposites would be defects, from which God is transcendent. This passage confirms the Ash‘arī position that God's attributes are not identical to His essence nor separate from it, but are real and eternal, distinct from the essence yet subsisting in it.

Key Terms
صفات المعاني
زائدة على الذات
كمالات
تنزيه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's attributes are either identical to His essence (as in Mu'tazilite thought) or completely separate entities (as in a crude understanding of attributes).
Correction: This passage affirms they are 'additional to the essence' (zāʼida ʻalā al-dhāt), meaning they are distinct in meaning and reality but not separate existences. They subsist in the essence as eternal perfections.

Checkpoint
What does the passage say about the relationship between God's attributes and His essence?
A) The attributes are identical to the essence
B) The attributes are additional to the essence and are distinct perfections
C) The attributes are temporary accidents
D) The attributes are the same as the actions of God

Key Takeaway
God's attributes are real, eternal, and distinct perfections subsisting in His essence, not mere conceptual aspects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You regularly call upon Allah as 'al-ʿAlīm' (the All-Knowing). But do you truly live as if His knowledge is a real, all-encompassing perfection that penetrates every corner of your life, including your secret thoughts? This week, before a single action, pause and say: 'Allah knows this.' Then act accordingly.
?
If God's attributes are real perfections, then His power and will are actively at work in your life right now. When you face a situation that feels out of control, do you instinctively trust that His power is real and sufficient, or do you rely on your own plans? Commit to surrendering one specific worry to His power this week.
?
The lesson declares that God's attributes are 'not by mere essence'. This means He is not a vague force but a personal Lord with distinct perfections. Do you find yourself relating to Allah as a distant concept or as a living, hearing, seeing, speaking reality? How would your prayer change if you spoke to Him as One who truly hears and speaks? Resolve to address Him by one of His attributes in your next prayer.

Allah's Speech is Not Sound or Letters
Ghazali negates physical attributes of Allah's speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Muslim theologians negate physical qualities from Allah's speech and the distinction between created speech (accidents) and divine speech (an eternal attribute).

Core Idea
Allah's speech is an eternal attribute, not a physical sound or letter.

Imam al-Ghazali starts his discussion by clearing away any anthropomorphic misconceptions about divine speech. He asserts that Allah's speech is not produced by physical processes like escaping air or colliding bodies, nor is it composed of letters formed by lip or tongue movements. This lesson examines that foundational negation and why it is necessary for a proper understanding of the Quran's eternity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note that it begins with a clear negation and then gives two specific examples.
2
Identify the two negations
Notice that Ghazali denies that divine speech is a sound produced by air or bodies, and denies that it is composed of letters formed by lips or tongue.
These are the most common ways humans produce speech.
3
Understand the rationale
Consider why these are denied: created speech is an accident (ʿaraḍ), but Allah's speech is not describable by body or accident. This is the key theological principle.
Accidents are temporary and in need of a substance; Allah is beyond that.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يشبه كلام الخلق ، فليس بصوت يحدث من انسلاخ هواء أو اصطكاك أجرام ، ولا بحرف ينقطع باطباق شفة أو تحريك لسان (۱) ، وأن القرآن والتوراة والانجيل والزبور كتبه المنزلة على رسله عليهم السلام (۲) ، وأن القرآن مقروء بالألسنة مكتوب في المصاحف ، محفوظ في القلوب (۳) ، وأنه مع ذلك قديم قائم بذات الله تعالى ، لا يقبل الانفصال والافتراق ، بالانتقال إلى القلوب والأوراق (٤) ، وأن موسى سمع كلام الله بغير صوت ولا حرف ، كما يرى الأبرار ذات الله تعالى في الآخرة (٥) من غير جوهر ولا عرض . (۱) إذ كلام الخلق كله عرض ، وكلام الله تعالى لا يوصف بجسم ولا عرض ، ولهذا بين الامام الغزالي رضي الله عنه وجه عدم شبهه كلام الخلق فقال : ه فليس بصوت يحدث من بين انسلاخ هواء ، أو اصطكاك أجرام ، ولا بحرف يتقطع باطباق شفة أو تحرك لسان ، فكل ذلك من صفات كلام الخلق (۲) لأن الحروف إنما هي عبارة عنه ، والعبارة غير المعبر عنه ، فلذلك اختلفت باختلاف الالسنة ، وإذا عبرت عن تلك الصفة القائمة بذاته تعالى بالعربية فقرآن ، وبالعبرانية فتوراة ، وبالسريانية فانجيل وزبور ، والاختلاف في العبارات دون المسمى ، فحروف القرآن حادثة والمعبر عنه بها هو المعنى القائم بذات الله تعالى قديم، فالتلاوة والقراءة والكتابة حادثة ، والمتلو والمقروء والمكتوب قديم . وبيان المراد : أن ما دلت عليه الكتابة والقراءة والتلاوة ، كما إذا ذكر الله بألسنة متعددة ولغات مختلفة فإن الذكر حادث والمذكور وهو رب العالمين قديم (۳) وفي نسخة أخرى : محفوظ في القلوب والصدور (٤) كما لا يقبل العدم ولا ما في معناه من السكوت ، ولا التجديد ، ولا البعض ولا الكل ، ولا التقديم ولا التأخير، ولا اللحن ولا الاعراب ، ولا سائر التغييرات (٥) رؤية تليق بذاته تعالى
It does not resemble the speech of creation; it is not a sound produced from the escape of air or the collision of bodies, nor a letter cut off by the closing of a lip or the movement of a tongue (1). And that the Quran, the Torah, the Gospel, and the Psalms are His revealed books sent down to His messengers, peace be upon them (2). And that the Quran is recited by tongues, written in mushafs, and preserved in hearts (3). And that despite that, it is eternal, subsisting by the essence of Allah Almighty, not subject to separation or division by transfer to hearts and pages (4). And that Moses heard the speech of Allah without sound or letter, just as the righteous will see the essence of Allah Almighty in the Hereafter (5), without substance or accident. (1) For the speech of creation is entirely accidental (ʿaraḍ), and the speech of Allah Almighty is not described as a body or accident; therefore Imam Ghazali, may Allah be pleased with him, explained the aspect of its dissimilarity to the speech of creation, saying: it is not a sound produced from the escape of air or the collision of bodies, nor a letter cut off by the closing of a lip or the movement of a tongue, for all that is among the attributes of the speech of creation. (2) Because letters are but an expression of it, and the expression is other than the expressed; therefore they differ according to the difference of tongues. When that attribute subsisting by His essence is expressed in Arabic, it is the Quran; in Hebrew, the Torah; in Syriac, the Gospel and Psalms. The difference is in the expressions, not in the named reality. So the letters of the Quran are created, while the expressed meaning subsisting by Allah's essence is eternal. Thus recitation (tilāwa), reading (qirāʾa), and writing are created, while the recited (al-matluww), the read (al-maqrūʾ), and the written (al-maktūb) are eternal. Clarification: what is indicated by writing, reading, and recitation is like when Allah is mentioned by multiple tongues and different languages—the mention is created, while the mentioned (al-madhkūr), who is the Lord of the worlds, is eternal. (3) In another copy: preserved in hearts and chests. (4) It does not accept non-existence nor what is in its meaning of silence, nor renewal, nor partiality nor totality, nor precedence nor delay, nor incorrect declension nor grammatical inflection, nor any other changes. (5) A vision befitting His essence.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal exposition on the nature of Allah's speech (kalām Allāh) and the eternal status of the Quran. The author, Imam al-Ghazali, begins by negating any resemblance between Allah's speech and human speech: it is not a sound produced by physical processes like air escaping or bodies colliding, nor is it composed of letters formed by lip closure or tongue movement. This is because the speech of creation is an accident (ʿaraḍ), while Allah's speech is not describable by body or accident. The footnote elaborates that Ghazali explicitly denies these physical characteristics. Next, he affirms that the Quran, Torah, Gospel, and Psalms are Allah's revealed books sent to His messengers. He then states that the Quran is recited, written in codices, and preserved in hearts, yet despite these created acts, it remains eternal and subsisting by Allah's essence, not subject to division or transfer. The second footnote clarifies that letters are mere expressions (ʿibārāt) of the eternal attribute; the expressions differ by language, but the expressed meaning (al-maʿnā al-qāʾim bi-dhāt Allah) is eternal. Thus the letters of the Quran are created, while the meaning is eternal. Recitation, reading, and writing are created acts, but that which is recited, read, and written (the eternal speech) is uncreated. The third footnote provides an alternate wording. The fourth footnote expands on the eternal nature: it does not accept non-existence, silence, renewal, partiality, totality, precedence, delay, incorrect grammar, or any changes. Finally, Ghazali states that Moses heard Allah's speech without sound or letter, analogous to the vision of Allah by the righteous in the Hereafter, which is without substance or accident—a vision befitting His essence, as the fifth footnote explains.

Key Terms
كلام الله
عرض
صوت
حرف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Allah's speech is like human speech but just more perfect.
Correction: Ghazali argues it is entirely different in kind, not just degree, because it is not composed of sounds or letters at all.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, Allah's speech is not a sound because:
A) It is too loud
B) It is not produced by physical processes
C) It is only in the heart
D) It is metaphorical

Key Takeaway
Allah's speech is fundamentally unlike created speech because it is not composed of physical sounds or letters.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you truly believe you are reciting the eternal speech of Allah, not just beautiful words? Does this belief change how you prepare your heart before recitation?
?
If Allah's speech is not sound or letters, what does that mean for your relationship with the Quran? Are you content with just the words, or do you seek the meaning behind them to connect with the eternal attribute?
?
How often do you reduce Allah's speech to a mere recitation competition or aesthetic experience, forgetting that it transcends all physical limitations? What will you do today to realign your reverence for the Quran with this truth?

The Quran: Eternal Meaning, Created Expressions
Ghazali affirms the eternity of the Quran despite its recitation and writing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran can be recited and written yet remain eternal, and the distinction between the eternal meaning and the created expressions.

Core Idea
The Quran's letters are created, but its meaning is eternal and subsists by Allah's essence.

After establishing that Allah's speech is not physical, Ghazali turns to the Quran itself. He affirms that the Quran, along with the Torah, Gospel, and Psalms, is Allah's revealed book. He then addresses a common confusion: how can the Quran be recited by tongues and written in mushafs yet still be eternal? This lesson explains the critical distinction between the expression (ʿibāra) and the expressed meaning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the four statements: revealed books, Quran recited/written, Quran eternal, and the negation of change.
2
Identify the apparent tension
The Quran is described as recited, written, and preserved in hearts, yet it is also said to be eternal. How can something physical (recitation, writing) be eternal?
This tension is resolved by the distinction between expression and meaning.
3
Understand the resolution
The footnote explains that the letters and recitation are created expressions (ʿibārāt) of the eternal meaning. The meaning itself is uncreated and subsists by Allah's essence.
The analogy: mentioning Allah in different languages—the mention is created, but the mentioned (Allah) is eternal.
4
Reflect on the negations
The eternal speech does not accept non-existence, silence, renewal, division, or grammatical changes. This emphasizes its transcendence.
